Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are in the fundament, one or more, and are old and consist of large cold and moist corrupt humors, and they have been treated according to what we have said in divisions but it is not helpful, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, that which is just behind the nape of the neck in a triangular fashion, and one cautery below the navel. Two days
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that his stomach is cooled down and the food does not digest well, and you see the face swollen, then make one great cautery on the stomach as it has been said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen at each clavicle cautery; leave the cautery on for a long time. Afterwards cleanse him until he is sound.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshy growth called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut a vein, heat the cautery that resembles a razor, and then place it burning on the cut vein. Leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the base of the vein where blood flows. Do this once or twice. If there is much flesh, cauterize each one as we have said. Afterwards, treat with ointments until they are clean. And if you cauterize a large vein with a hot cautery, it will have greater benefit.
de plaie mal curee	From poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	If the patient cannot tolerate incision or opening, which we will discuss later, then this disease comes about which cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If a fistula occurs and is inflamed and filled with putrid matter and corrupt moisture, you should probe it carefully throughout its entire length, ensuring that you know the full depth of the tunnel. After heating the cautery that resembles a razor, insert it into the fistula according to how deep the probe has gone, and continue applying the cautery until all the corrupted flesh is burned away, once or twice depending on what is needed. Be careful not to burn the nerves that are nearby, or the large veins. If the fistula leads to the bladder or intestines, be especially careful in those locations, and only perform the procedure in a crowded area, making sure it is not done openly. Afterward, treat the location until it is healed, and if the area becomes dry and the matter has been removed for some time, then know that the area is entirely healed. But if the matter has not been removed, know that the area is still infected and corrupt bone lies beneath; and thus we will discuss this further later on.
de la maladie des reins	About kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	If pain and coldness come upon the kidneys accompanied by great windiness, and there is no menstrual flow in women, then you should perform cautery on the kidneys on both sides with the cautionary iron that we have mentioned earlier. If we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, which will provide greater relief.

de la marris	of anger

de la hainche	of the beard

de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere. de la dolor des jointes	Of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pains are caused by moistures that have spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in the foot, which doctors properly call "podagra," and when it is from a cold cause and cannot be cured with medicines, then it can be cured by cautery in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:

And if it is necessary to touch the face of the foot, then make the cautery at all points that one calls a "point." de la routure dou syfac	It seems that you meant to ask about "la routeure du sacrum" which refers to the sacroiliac joint dysfunction. Here's how you can treat it according to an old French medical text:
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When gout comes to the ankles, and the bulls descend to the joints newly, it is necessary that when you see him curing, he should not chew anything that day; and let him use things that leave the belly so that the feces descend from his belly. Afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his tail until the eyes are repaired, then bind it with your two hands, and press firmly under the gout near the bone of the wrist, and there is a sign like half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery which is here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Heat the cautery until it is white and emits sparks. Then replace the bowels in their place; and let the attendant hold his hand so that they do not return backwards; and open the thighs of the patient well, and put one cushion under him and one servant on the thighs, and another on the chest to hold the hands; then put the cautery on the sign with your whole hand, holding it with your right hand and your left until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, repeat it again until you reach the bone. And be careful that the eye does not jump out when you perform the cautery; so that you do not burn it; and that by this the patient does not die or suffer some other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing. And it is necessary that the cauteries for children are subtle according to their size, and for large people they should be large according to theirs. After three days, cure the place of the cautery with butter until the blister is removed; then cure him with other ointments until he is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bindings are loosened gradually, so that the eye does not jump out when he gets up to go to bed.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, provide him with a well-made splint and keep it on for another forty days; and let him have good rest, so that he does not tire himself out too much and be careful not to overeat or drink too much, or laugh too loudly. And when this instruction is followed, he will be entirely healed. And I will speak later about the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Chapter on Laparotomy
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When laparotomies occur in other bellies and are recognized, and you see that they are no longer growing, perform one cautery with the cautery according to its size, and burn the third of the heart; then cure it according to what we have said earlier; and some of the ancients say that it should be cauterized at three angles in this shape:

de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of old pain in some limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to some limb, whether from falling or hitting it, and this pain lasts a long time, and the remedies of medicine are not effective, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cautery should be applied according to the length of the limb, its thickness, its weakness and strength, its location in terms of twists, and the severity of the pain. If one cautery is insufficient, another should be repeated on top of it, because it is customary for them to move closer to the member that is nearest to it, so you must apply cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	"Of dislocations"
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. "Wounds are sometimes cauterized by fire with great caution, and especially the disease that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	"And if the dislocation is spread everywhere and it is clearly apparent, then you should cauterize it with these cauteries that we have mentioned on top: one at the nape of the neck, and two on the spine of the neck, and six on the spine of the back, and one large one on the hip and another near it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are behind the heel; and sometimes one cautery is made on the bone of the wrist, and one on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver."
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	"And know that the more cauteries you do, the more help you give and the more benefit it provides. And know that sick people do not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because the body is already completely corrupted. And be sure that the cauteries are large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of iron tools. Afterward, cure the place with flour of vervain with honey and other remedies until it is healed."
de enfleure	Here's a possible translation for "de enfleure" which is Old French:
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling occurs in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but it is not completely gone, then apply fire cauteries to the limb according to its size; let the cautery penetrate a bit into the space of the heart; then treat with ointments until it is healed. And sometimes cauteries are applied to the hand, foot, back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; yet no one should meddle in this if they are not knowledgeable about limbs and the exits of moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of Albarras
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the illness called "albaras" is advanced and remedies of medicine are ineffective, then cauterize with a cautery that penetrates somewhat deeply, according to the quantity of the space of the heart until the swelling is removed and its color is changed; then treat with flour of vetches and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of a pigeon and blood of an owl, each one part; and mix it all together, and tie it up in a cloth, and apply it to the place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	For the cure of chancre by cautery:
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When a chancre appears at the beginning and you see it stopping, then cauterize it with a cautery that resembles one circle, all around the edge of the chancre. And indeed wise men say that one should also make a cautery in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen before; and it is more advisable that it be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circule," as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of swelling that cannot subside
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has an illness called "adubelati," and it is slow to subside, either because of the excessiveness that it causes or because of the water from the patient when they are decrepit (that is, too old) and have little blood, or because of the air; and you see it hastening to subside: then cauterize it around with many small cauteries in prickling; afterwards leave it thus. For it will hasten to subside.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	"And if you wish to pierce it entirely with the cautery, heat the cautery which is described here:"
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	"And place your hand on the middle of this disease called 'adubelati' until the cautery has pierced the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it going out in such a way that the course of corruption is alleviated. After the cure, when it is completely healthy."
li cure dou feu par fer	"The cure by fire with iron"
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	"There is another disease called 'corrodens', which is nothing but a consumption of limbs, for it consumes the limbs just as fire consumes dry logs. If you see this disease in a place that can tolerate cautery together with fire, then heat the cauteries, both small and large, according to what is necessary for the location where the disease is; after that, cauterize all over until you have eradicated all corruption, and let nothing remain of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed. And leave it alone for three days, and put on the cauterized places a poultice made with oil until the burns from the fire are healed, and all corruption. After the cure of ointments that generate flesh. And if after three days healthy flesh does not appear, then begin again with the cautery on what remains of the corrupted places. And this consumption has sometimes been cured by an acidic medicine in place of a fire cautery; but nevertheless, a fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure of the acidic medicine in the division: take as much as you need."
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	"of swellings that come on the feet"
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	**A sickness called "clos" often arises in the feet due to defects, which is a large, broken thing that wounds the foot. There are two ways to cauterize this disease: fire cautery and hot water cautery.**
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are turned away from the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you must bring cautery of hot water; and it is done thus: take a reed cane or one made of iron, or a goose feather, and place it on the nail and the flesh, that is to say on warts; and place the cane so that it encircles all around, then put some hot water in, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the cane reaches the root of the nail, and can find a deep path for the hot water to reach the root; and let the patient endure a little the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will deroot itself completely with all its roots. Do this one after another until you have uprooted all those that are on the body, then treat them with ointments that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	And the treatment for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone is trembling from coldness of the nerves, or from quartan fever or other fever, then you should make for them four cauteries or five on the spine of the back, one between each spine; and one on the foot, and one on the stomach at the olive-shaped cautery; this will stop the trembling, and the health of the body will be restored from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	And of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes it is apparent on the outside of the body, where baths appear or smelly pustules come from large corrupted matters. So when they first appear, one must perform a cauterization on each head of the pustule: a fine cautery of myrtle wood, whose point has been heated in fire, or long root of aloe, or lenticular cautery. And sometimes they cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow further from then on, but the excesses whence they come are broken up, and they are made clean; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When an artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great flows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the outside, or at the incision of the boil, or at the cautery of the member, and in similar things; and it is very difficult to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And moreover when this happens to anyone, one should quickly place their two index fingers on the wound's opening and press very hard until the blood is pacified beneath your fingers and no more drops come out; then put on the fire olive oil cauteries of various sizes both large and small until they are all red hot; then take either a large or small cautery according to the wound and the place where the artery runs, and place the cautery upon that vein where you hold your fingers, holding it there until the bleeding stops.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if blood suddenly flows forth when you lift your fingers from the wound and the cautery has expired, quickly take another one of the cauteries that are on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after another until the bleeding is stopped. And take care that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the sick person. And know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well stopped except by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction if it is not too large, or by tightly binding a thread, or by medicines applied that have power to stop bleeding; and let it be bound and pressed appropriately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about stopping by tying very tightly with cloths or putting hot things upon it, or similar things, it profits little if at all.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he has neither surgeon nor medicine present, one should place their index finger on the wound's opening as we have said, and press very hard until it is stopped above the wound and the vein; and do not move your finger, but moisten it with cold water often and make it very cold until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped. And then do what is necessary with cauteries and medicines afterward.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the remedies for wounds
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	In the first chapter we have told you about every disease in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire or hot medicine, and the causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; and I have placed that chapter at the beginning for ease of finding what one wants. And now I will go along the same path in this chapter so that one may find more easily what they desire.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And before I begin this chapter, dear friend, you should know that in this one there is more danger and fear than in the first about cauteries, and therefore greater caution is necessary.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the practice of this chapter there are many times evacuations of blood when opening wounds and making incisions on boils and treating wounds, and extracting splinters and making incisions on stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many people die thereby.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	"And I advise you not to undertake foolishness. For many kinds of people come for treatment, some of whom are so attached to their illness that they die easily due to the recklessness they find in their condition and the severity of their ailment; one should fear these."
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	"There are those who give up their reason and say: 'Wait, I am cured'; but the disease is deceitful. It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but rather place greater care in your honor than in your avarice, and do not open yourself foolishly but wisely to those from whom you are certain and whom you can have taken and praised; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients for their salvation to be achieved; and this will help you acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise."
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear beloved son, May Our Lord grant you good understanding and uprightness, and if He wishes to inspire you with His holy breath, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	"Or I have arranged this chapter in sections, dividing it into chapters according to what is before the chapter on cauteries that I have already divided from head to toe, so that you may find more easily those things of which you will have need."
dou chief plein d’aigue	"head full of water"
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	**Know that this ailment often comes to children at birth, and when the mother squeezes too hard on the child's head; sometimes it happens due to an unknown cause.**
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	**And I have never seen this ailment happen outside of children, and for all those that I have seen, the jaw is dislocated; therefore it seems to me that it would be best if I left aside the rest of my work in such cases.**
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	**And I saw one child whose head was full of water, and each day it swelled so much that he could hardly bear it; and the swelling increased so much that it reached the mouth, and this swelling is collected beneath the bone above the spleen, between the heart and the bone; and if the swelling is between the heart and the bone, and the tumors are small, you should make a cut in the head that is wide, and as long as two fingers, wherever the swelling reaches. Here is the shape of the spatula:**
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	**If the swelling is greater, and the tumors are larger, then make two cuts in the shape of a cross, like this:**
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	**And if the swelling is beneath the bone, and you see that the angles of the head are raised on each side, and water gushes out when you press it with your hand inside, but there is no response: then you must make three cuts in the head in this manner:**
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	**And after the incision, remove all the swelling from outside. Then bind the cuts with cloths and powders, and put wine and oil on them, leaving it like that until the fifth day; then untie it, and cure the wound with tents and ointments, and let the head be bandaged evenly, and give the sick person dry food to eat, taking away a little bit of the swelling each time until the member is healed.**
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	**And another way of incision is to look where the greatest part of the tumor opens and where the water is collected; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.**
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	**Therefore cut where the tumor opens and where the water is collected, and make the incision according to what you can do; but beware that you do not cut the artery; for if a vein bleeds profusely, then the patient will die from loss of blood and evacuation of swelling.**
de reume	**de reume**
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When one has a disease called "catarra" in the eyes or the foot, and the disease is chronic, and medical treatment does not help at all, then the final remedy is fire cauteries with the application of two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when cauterizing the eyes, you should first have the patient lie down on their back; then scrub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries appear. After that, tie the patient's neck with one cloth. Then look for where the veins are located, and the places of both are near the ears, but they are usually hidden. After marking these areas with incisions, cauterize each one with a spatula heated to two parts using forceps until the cut reaches the bone, and this should be done along the width of the skull.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, place the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting about two fingers' width across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	Once the vein is severed, blood flows out continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the artery does not open to touch, you must measure a space of three fingers' width, then press down and cut until you reach the bone; and about six ounces of blood should flow out, perhaps a bit more or less depending on what the patient can endure and how full the artery is. Then examine the wound: if there is any point of syphilis remaining on the bone, carefully remove it with tweezers, then press the wound shut and bind it, applying ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	de emigrainne
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient migraine comes on, and catarrh is present due to the moistness of tears and heat in the temples, causing ancient madness and similar symptoms, even when treated with various remedies, if no improvement is seen, then extract the arteries from the temples using cauterization, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The manner of extracting them is that the patient should shave the hair from their temples and locate the artery which opens into the temple, for it is quite visible due to its pulsating motion, although in some people who are very cold it may be less apparent. If it is not apparent, the patient should wrap a cloth around the neck to restrict blood flow, then rub the area with a coarse cloth and wash it with warm water until the artery becomes clearly visible. Then take the spatula shaped as follows:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then carefully scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then lift it with pincers and separate it from the surrounding tissue on both sides. If the artery is small, twist it off with a needle point, then cut that section according to the thickness of two fingers' width. For if it is not cut, all the blood will not flow out at once.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw six drops of blood until three; and if the artery is large, then you should tie it in two places with a strong silk thread so that corruption does not come before the wound heals, and let blood flow freely; then cut away the excess flesh between the two ties at this same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize with a cutting cautery until the bone is reached; and this is the main work, if the patient has no fever and is of warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery aids in finishing moisture: therefore it is of greater aid against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where, for the extraction of arteries, one should fill the place with old cotton and put on well-made dressings; and when they are removed, cure them with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and dressings, until it is healed. And if blood flows from the artery as many times as you work there, hasten to cauterize with a copper cautery, or fill the place with vitriol and hold your hand steady until the blood is stanched; and if this is not present, put your fist on the place until the blood congeals, and wash the place with cold water until the blood stops, and press it as it should be. And that which is quicker and lighter in extracting an artery is to cauterize the vein with a cutting cautery of two parts, but let the cuts be well spaced to retain heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	But when the instruments are too thin, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be a space of one finger's width between the two knives, and then when you have marked both places with incisions, and you measure with the heated iron until it reaches the bone, cut the vein at both places; and they should be distant between the two incisions for this cautery is not continuous throughout. And this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are above the forehead of the head, and it does not help to apply medicine there, and you see the face becoming redder, and feel on the forehead a trembling as if from shivering; and if the eyelids are thin and moist so that the hairs of the eyelashes have fallen out, and the eyelashes are heated and scraped by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And the ancients called this treatment "treatment for contusion," and it is as follows: When you treat a patient who has this disease, first pluck the hairs from their forehead, then make three incisions on the forehead equally spaced according to its length; one of these incisions should be two fingerbreadths long in the middle of the forehead down towards the nose, and the other two should be two fingerbreadths long each, above the eyelids, and you must guard against cutting the arteries that are located on either side above the eyelids; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and each wound should be three fingers wide across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have ready a sponge and many cloths to wipe away the blood, then place the spatula heated with two parts of this mixture on it:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	And scrape away all the skin that is between the two incisions down to the temple bone, then remove this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Then insert into the first incision an instrument called a "cultellarium," which is very sharp on one side and smooth on the other without being sharp; this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And insert the cutting edge of the cultellarium towards the flesh near the heart, and its smooth side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle incision. Then cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes as far as the incision opens onto the heart, then do the same in the middle incision up to the other one; then drain out the blood equally, and compress the area for bleeding. Then place a pad of old cotton in each incision, and put on wet cloths with vinegar, oil, and salt, and make sure that no pus enters. And on the third day remove the stitches, and apply great abundance of cold water, then treat with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	Of the treatment of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	If catarrh often comes upon you, and you see the eyelids thin and small, and your vision is weakened, and the eyelashes are burned; and the hairs fall out, and deep pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know by these symptoms that this matter and this catarrh come from many veins, and the cure for it is this:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it is as follows: Command the patient to lie on their back, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead and another one fingerbreadth wide. Begin at the left temple incision to the right temple, and let the incision go down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves that move during chewing; and when the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, then open up between the two lips of the incision and put in old cotton and linen pads. Then tie on wet cloths with vinegar and oil, and guard against hot pus; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow there, then treat it with drying agents that cause flesh to grow.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, mix them together, and apply this plaster to these wounds to stimulate the growth of flesh everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the blocking of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things:
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it falls into the ear stone or some other thing that does not fit the ear nor grow in it, put the ear to the sun. If you see the stone, distill a little drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then bring about extraction; and when the sneeze comes, hold his nose with a cloth or wool around the ear; and let the ear be raised up. Often fire comes from this treatment; and if it does not come, bring about extraction with fine forceps, of which here is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it does not come out with forceps, that is good; if not, bring about extraction with a fine needle of small thickness. And if it does not come out that way, make a cane of straw and put the head of the cane into the hole of the ear strongly, and stop up what is around the cane with soft wax so that wind cannot enter with the cane; then draw fire very vigorously, for often fire comes in this manner as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take glutinous substance which birds use, and put some on an instrument which is sharp for this purpose, and put a little cotton around; then press the glut on the stone or whatever thing it may be, and draw fire.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear before aposteme comes and spasm. And the manner of cutting is this: first let the sick person be bled from the cephalic vein according to his strength, then make the sick person sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small crescent-shaped cut in the root of the ear where it depends; then pull out the stone according to your power, and suck it quickly into your mouth. And continue the treatment until he is cured.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and the ear becomes swollen, bring about extraction accordingly. And if it cannot come out, bring about extraction with a thin, subtle spatula according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And bring about incision of that grain. But do not perform this when you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with fine forceps and by suction, as we have said, so that the extraction may be complete.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Therefore, when water falls into the ear it is necessary for the sick person to use sneezing and plug the ear with old cotton. And let them lie on that same ear where the water is. If it comes out by itself, that is good. But if not, take many stones according to the length of your forearm, thin and light, and heat them a little in the fire; and put one into the sick person's ear opening, and strike with another stone from outside on that side, and hit one stone against another so that the water comes out completely, and thus it will all come out. And if you see, take a reed, and put one end of it in the ear, and put the other end into the fire until that part of the reed is burned; then repeat with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said with the stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it is small-bodied, such as a flea or something similar, treat it as we have said in the division. But if it is large-bodied so that you can feel it, bring about extraction with forceps; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of earthworms in ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in treating distillations, and if the treatment does not help, it is necessary to examine the ear in sunlight: if any worms are visible, extract them with fine forceps; but if they cannot be seen, take the pipe of which this form is here:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And it should be narrow below and wide above. And place the most subtle head into the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the sick person, then suck firmly along the entire tube; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey in coming out, then stop up around the tube with cotton as I have said for the stone; and if they still do not leap forth as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the killing of worms, and you will find them in treatises on distillations; and thus distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, of which this is the form as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be of silver or bronze narrow below with a small hole, and above open for distillation; and for pressing within the distillation, one well-made brass instrument for this purpose, and if you wish take one razor and wrap cotton around its point neatly; then pour your oil or juice, and what you wish of your medicines into the tube, and the tube should be in the ear; then place within the razor with all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled cleanly from the ear; and let the patient feel it within, and let the distillation be one small heated vessel on the fire beforehand when it is distilled into the ear; and guard that it not be too cold, for the medicine will not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Here is an illustration of the instrument described in the text:
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in their ears; the same thing happens to adults due to injury of the ear or flesh growing inside it, and these blockages sometimes occur deep within the ear so that one cannot see them; sometimes there is only partial obstruction of the hole.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when it occurs deep within the ear so that one cannot see it, it is difficult to treat in many ways. But in cases where you can see the obstruction, you should place the patient's ear in the sun and look inside: if you see the dark spot clearly, then perform the operation described below:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and cutting before and behind entirely full, so that it does not wound the ear; if the obstruction is of flesh born in the body of the ear, hold it with fine pincers, and cut it lightly, until all that flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the obstruction is deeply inside the ear, then take one sharp razor and heat it slightly over the fire, and then place it on the body of the ear. If you feel the obstruction which the patient feels pain when hearing, cut it lightly, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a tampon according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or else take a tampon and moisten it with rosewater, and sprinkle powdered vitriol upon it. And if you see that the ear is swollen, then it is necessary to remove the tampon and replace it with another one moistened in cerote which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling has subsided; then cleanse it until it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is a discharge of blood coming out, then plunge a sponge wrapped in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the flow of blood which are found in treatises on distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the flesh of pears
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the remedy that comes from the flesh of pears when they are moist and then become dry: you should stretch them with forceps and pincers, and cut it with a scalpel at its roots; then sprinkle powdered vitriol on it.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they continue to grow without being cut down, then cauterize them with a lenticular cautery instrument, and the cauterizing afterwards cuts off more of their roots. And often they need to be retreated several times because some thing remains from their roots; but when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not grow back again.
de la gresle	Of hailstones
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times there come up on the skin certain things that resemble hailstones in their shape and hardness, and because of this disease is called "hail," and it is a collection of moisture hardened above and below the paper. The treatment for this is as follows: observe if the hail moves from one side to the other, and this is an easy thing to know. Then make the incision wide enough, then scrape off each part lightly, then take it with pincers and cut it out. If you cannot cut it out without piercing a little bit of the skin, do not worry about the patient; and if the opening is large, then sew it up with stitches, and treat it until it is healed; but if it is small, do not apply any pressure, for ointments will soon restore it and make new flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hail is descending into the ear towards the upper part, then turn the skin and stretch it with pincers and cut out the hail, pressing on both sides. If the skin is stretched by the incision, do not worry about it; but once the hail has been cut out, rinse the wound with salt water, and treat it with ointment that brings new flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat of the ears
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Eczema is a grease that appears on the skin of the ears above, and this happens more in children than in adults, and it causes great discomfort to their ears. And they have catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at sunlight because tears rush to their eyes. And so they often lie on their faces, sleeping on them, and their skin under their eyebrows is moist with exudate and appears reddened and inflamed by the eczema that appears in the eye. And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the eczema between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of treatment is as follows: the patient should put their head in your hand. Then take one linen cloth and prepare it like a circle according to the quantity that contains the eczema on each part. Then place it over them and press with your fingers on both sides so that the eczema collects within the circle. Then make an incision in the middle of the moisture with a scalpel, making it no larger than the wound made for bleeding. And cut deep into the skin until you reach the eczema. And in several positions, eczema will come out of the incision, resembling a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then extract all at once with a piece of cloth between your fingers, squeezing it back and forth from left to right until it is dispersed. And be careful not to squeeze too hard against the incision so that you do not draw out the scalpel or cause bleeding.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	"And if the exit does not open at the beginning of the slit, then slightly widen the slit lightly until it opens; then extract as we have said, then soak cloths in warm water and vinegar, and place them on the wound, and bind with bandages."
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if there are men who grind flax and put it on to corrupt the moisture that has remained. Then cover it until it is healed. And if inflammation comes to the wound, then cure it with gentle poultices until it heals."
des poilz des papieres	"of the hairs of papers"
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	"When hairs grow on papers besides their natural ones and are entwined, they harm the eyes and cause diseases like habitual tears and softening of the papers and opacity, to such an extent that it causes destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways to treat it: either by cauterization with fire together, or by hot medicine according to what is written in the cautery chapter, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by caustics, depending on what I will say."
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	"It is necessary that you place the head of the sick person in your lap, then turn the paper away from the eye with your left hand; if it turns, it's good; if not, insert a needle at one thread above it; and whether it is near the edge of the paper or where the hairs are growing next to these hairs, and draw one thread up along the entire paper, and turn it towards the razor; then cut into the part below the paper, below the attached hairs, with all the spatula coping, from the large larmier to the small; then extract one thread, and place a small tent of cotton and cloth under the paper, then press on the paper with an incense burner, like a mirror glass, and in any case, the figure should be according to the quantity that you see raising the paper that is divided into two."
