Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	"And if one has need to cut a large quantity of paper according to how much the paper is softened; then cut with the spatula all along the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the large larmier to the small; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert an awl into one of the two angles of the heart, then scrape it all; then bring the two lips together with a stitch of an awl with one thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and let dry the excess threads on the two eyebrows with any gluey things you see fit to do; and if not, pay no mind to it, then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without stitching with drying and tightening things, for paper revives at the union of the wound and its assembly, but stitching is mute (as the ancients said), and this is a useless work."
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	"And there is another way: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure like this one of the incense burner, as we have said before, with three circles divided according to the shape that is here:"
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	"Then cut what is above the small circles evenly according to the shape that is here:"
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you lack the power to hold the tweezers, and the thing is not even, then take a needle with one thread, and insert it into the figure; and insert another thread beside the large tear, and the second thread beside the small one, and assemble the threads evenly between your two fingers; then raise your hand evenly, and raise all the skin over what you have marked, as we have explained, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and care for it until it is healthy; and if an abscess forms at your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar softening ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes it happens that the hairs of the paper are converted [turned], so you must use what we have said about the incision, but stitching in one and the other is more skillful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The care of the canines is in this form: and it is that you turn the paper and make the cut inside according to what I have said, then make two canines by art, and two thin threads as long as the paper and the width of the spatula; then cut at the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other finely on top of the paper of the eye, and strain the two canines from the two parts firmly; leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will wrinkle and harden and whiten, until it shrinks by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long, then cut with some force, and care for it until it is healthy; and when the wound has healed, remove the paper, and the hairs will no longer point; this is the shape of the two canines that you should make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The procedure is as follows: Take a fine needle and insert one thread of soft, thin silk; then tie the ends together finely, and let the length of the threads be a palm long. Then prepare another thin silk thread briefly, and tie its end to the threads; then have the patient place his head in your hand, and stand near the sun so that the procedure is clear, for it is a subtle and fine procedure. Then insert the needle all the way into the hairline next to the root of the hair, and pierce it quickly through the paper until you pull it out above the natural hair; then pull the hair up to the chase, and insert that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand back so that all the hairs come out of the chase into the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase has been completed but the hairs do not come out with it, then pull the chase down from underneath all the thread that you have prepared, until the chase comes out of the hole above and you can see it with your eye; then pull the chase and the thread, close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and flesh grows over it. And if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the natural eyebrows and lift it up with that one, so that it is separated and then lifted up.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the rottenness of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or rottenness occurs in the eye, there are two ways it can happen: one natural and the other unnatural. It happens suddenly from a wound, cut, or cautery, or from similar causes.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	The manner of treating it is to cut open that scab and open the lips of the sore, and put in linen wicks until it heals. Do not use anything drying or constricting in its treatment, as this would make the disease worse than before. Instead, use softening things like fenugreek; rosewater or aloe and linseed cooked together; and ointments made from diacylon melted in some oil. Take one of these wicks and apply it to the cure of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	The goal of this treatment is to ensure that the wound does not heal in the same shape as it was before. The treatments we have mentioned are only remedies for this disease and not a guarantee that it will not return in its original form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of flesh coming into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease called "axacrati," which truly exists beneath that is natural but also accidental. The accident comes from wounding or splitting, cautery or similar things. Its treatment is as follows: Take a needle with a double thread and insert it into the flesh, making it pierce from the left eye towards the right until the thread appears on both sides of the flesh. Then lift the flesh upwards along the entire needle, and cut it with one broad spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that is good. But if not, take a razor and place it in the cut, then turn the paper over and make two cuts along its edges within the paper. Make the openings of these two cuts at the two angles of the incision you have made, forming an angle so that when assembled, the shape resembles the letter "Γ" (gamma) in Greek script. Then remove that piece of flesh according to the size of its edges and what is beneath it from the part covering the paper. Next, join the two separated parts and sew them together with a thread of wool. Then apply the cure as we have said earlier using softening medicines and wicks until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a cut or stitches or cautery, you should make a full-length incision under the hairs of the paper, following what was said earlier. Then separate the two leaves of a wick between them, as I have described before. The operation must be done according to the shape of the disease, for it is very varied in form. Skilled masters devise various means with all their power to make the figure return to its natural shape. And the sick person himself, according to what is needed in treatment and instruments, may vary his operations in many ways.
dou soudement de la papiere	Regarding the sudden tearing of paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this sudden tearing happens to many people in such a way that the paper above is stuck with the white of the eye, and cannot move nor perform its natural operations, then you must insert the point of a razor under the paper and lift it upwards. Then stretch it with tweezers until you cut what is stuck with a fine spatula that is neither too large nor too sharp, so that the sick person cannot bear if the spatula were too large or scratched the eye. Make your incision light so that the paper returns to its natural shape. Remove all that was stuck and sometimes apply saltwater to the eye, then rinse it with fresh water and collyrium. Then place a linen wick between the paper and the eye, and put wet wool moistened in egg yolk on the eye. After the third day, use collyrium and other warming substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Regarding the corner of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the corner of the eye can appear in two ways: one is nervous and resembles a hard, dry skin; the other is not nervous but resembles a moist, congealed blister. When touched with iron or attempted to be grasped with tweezers, it cannot be taken. Both kinds start near the large tear duct and gradually increase until they cover all of the eye's vision and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	The manner of incision is as follows: the patient places their head in your hand, then opens their eyes. You lift the paper with your hand and coil the corner with tweezers of fine double edge, stretching it upwards. Then take a needle and attach one horse hair or cow hair or ox hair to it, along with a strong thread. Double the point of the needle slightly and insert it into the corner, pushing it through entirely. Tie the corner with a thread and stretch it upwards. Remove all of the skin along the side of the corner that covers the pupil and sclera up to the head using a fine spatula and small forceps. Leave the natural tissue in the tear duct so that tears can flow naturally after the incision. Sometimes, the corner is stretched only with tweezers and thread, as mentioned earlier. Then remove it entirely with a soft spatula of this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And make sure that the spatula does not touch the delicate tissue and tear it, nor should the pupil be pierced. After the incision, sprinkle some crushed mallow on the eye and apply collyrium made from litargirum, leaving it overnight. Then treat as necessary until healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the corner is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle nor can tweezers grasp it, many times this kind of corner is cured with medicines. As I have mentioned in the division, they appear like this, and if you see one that needs to be removed, open the eye of the patient and use a light spatula shaped like this:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the finger gently, and if you see it does not decrease in width and reason presses on it, then distill from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litharge and red ochre and crushed salt, and stop up the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same operation, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But if something opposes you in the eye, such as an inflamed sore, then use milk, and first cure the hot sore until it is healthy; then resume the operation as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of flesh in the eye causes great harm to the eye, then suspend it from a goat's horn and cut off a portion of it, but not all, so that tears do not come forth; then distill into the eye red collyrium made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows on the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	There are sometimes some people for whom red flesh grows and covers the pupil, restricting sight and turning it towards death, appearing like a rose of balm; and the operation is this: the sick person places their head in your hand, then opens their eyes, and coil all that flesh onto suitable tweezers, and hold it with force; then cut off the first flesh, and keep cutting with a razor until the end, but take care not to injure the eye during the operation. And let the incision of the skin be as we have said in the incision of the fingernail, and with small forces like those used to remove a tooth, as the figure shows after this chapter;
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is completed and all the flesh removed, then fill the eye with powdered mallow or distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines into it, and put cotton soaked in egg white onto the eye afterwards, so that it is sure to be free from inflammation; and if something remains and hot pain increases, and you suspect inflammation, then leave the eye and cure the inflammation with things that calm inflammation; then return to your operation until it is healed, and do thus for every piece of flesh attached to the eye in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless, it is necessary that you alleviate the cure of each weak eye by natural means; and as for accidental cases, perform surgery with iron; and do not put your hand into any of these operations until you see that these members can endure this operation.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	There are red veins that cover the eye and hinder sight in their operation, continually weakening the eye every day. It is therefore necessary at first to examine whether the eye in which the sebaceous cyst has appeared is prominent, and there is no other visible disease except for the sebaceous cyst; then coil it in this manner: command the sick person to place their head in your hand, then suspend those veins onto suitable tweezers according to their wisdom, and let the tweezers be double like this figure:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And there shall be two onions placed degree by degree in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then twist these onions subtly with force, and squeeze the blood afterwards one after another until you see those veins move outside of the eye. Be careful not to cut the eye with the points of the tweezers, and perform this task at midday before the sun, and be very careful in your work so that you only affect those veins. Once you have done this, distill green and red vitriol oil into the eye to corrupt what remains of the sebaceous material.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	"And if you are unable to capture all of them at that time,
de la fistule de l’oil	Fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeon calls a fistula of the eye «arissati». When you cure it using cauterization and hot medicine according to what I have said before, but it is not healed, there must be something inside that makes you cut open the boil where it should burst, and drain all the moisture that is there until the bone becomes visible.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone becomes visible and you see corruption and blackness there, then prepare all the instruments of which this is the shape; it is called «aspre chief» (sharp head), and should be made of iron with one blunt end, and should be pointed like a file as it appears in the present shape
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the bone that is corrupted, then twist it between your two fingers and press down a little until you know that all the corruption has been removed. Do this several times, then apply medicinal powders to dry out the wound.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is healed and flesh grows back, and the body of the brow is healed, and remains like this for 40 days, and it does not recur or form a boil, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed. But if not, there is only one other remedy: to bring the fistula back to the opening of the tear duct according to this shape. And this is what you do: uncover the bone for the second time with iron and hot medicine, and when it has been uncovered take a probe in this form, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and let the shaft be tapered all the way to its tip as you see here
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place the probe on the bone near the lachrymal gland and move your hand away from the eye a little bit, then turn the entire probe until it pierces the bone. The sick person will feel this because they will feel wind entering their nose if they hold their hand over it. Then apply medicinal powders to dry out the wound, as I have taught you before. And when flesh grows back and the wound heals, the matter will go to the tear duct; so it is an easier thing for the sick person.
de l’issue de l’oil	Regarding the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the eye opens wide all around and nothing disturbs the nose or makes it smaller, then you must bandage the sick person. Then wash them, then place cupping glasses on their head without pricking them to suck out the blood. Then put a poultice made of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcolac on the eye, then compress the eye and cover it with bandages and cloths. And the manner of the cloths is as follows: take soft cloths and double each one four times, then place them on top of each other according to the amount that the eye needs. Then compress it firmly with a hard bandage from above, and then recommence the cupping glasses without pricking to suck out the blood. Then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye compressed day and night. And if the poultice melts, you must remove it. Then remove the poultice after the day and night, and if you see that the eye is healing, that is good. But if not, then recommence the compressing and bandages and poultice and cupping glasses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Regarding the rupture of a blood vessel in the eye
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a rupture occurs in the blood vessel of the eye and it opens and blood comes out like a grain of resin, and it is frightening to see. Then if you see this happen, do as follows: take a needle and insert it into the root of the lower part of the eye up to the upper part. Then take another needle with a doubled thread at the lachrymal gland area and make it pierce there, leaving the first needle in place. Then tie one part of the uve around with the doubled thread and compress it well. Then remove the needle and place wet linen dipped in egg yolk on the eye. Leave it until the blood coagulates with the uve. Then treat the eye with comforting substances until the wound is healed. And sometimes the wound is constrained by the uve on each side with a circle of cloth until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye has a large appearance, then pierce it with a thin spatula that comes out from deep within the eye and remove the moist albugo and let the eye descend, and enter in as quickly as possible. Then remove it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Regarding the bowing of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alacunnati" is nothing but the bowing of the eye that is gathered together in the eye, resembling descending water, but it is not water. And the manner of the appearance of this remedy is as follows: make the sick person sit on a well-prepared and upright seat. Then take their head between your hands on both sides and turn it until you see the bowing coming up above your eyes. Then have them fix their gaze and let them look down so that the light does not shake, and let the sick person see things as they usually do. And if it does not descend below, know that it is water. But if the descending of the bowing is not prepared as we have said, then make the sick person sit between your hands and take a thin spatula and pierce through the corneal tissue at one point along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal tissue and the crown until the bowing comes out. And when it has come out, distill hot water mixed with honey or fenugreek boiled in water and honey into the eye. Then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Regarding the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the likenesses of arrows in division, and those that should be pierced; we perform accordingly to health. You must make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from sunlight, and let them close their sound eye tightly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or right hand if it's right; then take with your right hand, if the eye is left, the tool called "almagda", or left hand if it's right; then put the point of the tool near the crown by the thickness of a ray on that inflammation of the eye at the lesser lachrymal part, then drive the tool called "almagda" virtuously until it pierces into the inflammation of the eye and feels that almagda reaches the empty thing; and the measure of the way almagda should be to the depth of the measure of the space which is from the plum to the end of the blackness; and that's the crown of the eye, so you will see the bone through that paper because of the brightness of the corneal cloth, then put the tool until it reaches where the arrow is, then press it under one way after another. If the arrow descends now, the patient will see before them and the tool in their eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a brief pause, if the arrow rises again along the second path, insert your finger with the tool; when it is completely inserted and does not rise further, remove almagda gently by rotating your hand little by little; then put a drop of silkworm gem on the eye, and wipe the eye clean. Then place a cloth soaked in rose oil and egg white over the eye to protect it, and tie it with the sound eye. Nowadays, we and those of our time usually put common powder with egg white on top.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, as there are some men whose eyes are too hard, you must take the tool called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce only the conjunctiva and not too deep, but make it one subtle little opening, then insert almagda as we have said; and when the work is complete, prepare for the patient a suitable bed in which they can sleep on their back in a dark room; and keep them from all movements, and let them eat light foods, and not move their head to the right or left, and tie them according to their condition for three days; then untie them in that same dark house, and test their sight, and when you make them see some things, then retie them until the seventh day. And it is not necessary that you do this during the time of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you do this afterwards, for the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If abscess occurs before the seventh day, untie the eye and apply treatment for soothing the inflammation; when it has subsided, then release the sight and place a plaster on the face to cover it for a few days, and keep them in that same dark house. Then gradually leave the house, and let them return to their usual habits. And know that no disciples should interfere with this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And there came to us one from the land of Iraq who told us that in their country they used almagda to pierce, and then suck out the water, but nevertheless I have never seen any such thing in our land nor read about it in the books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And here are the likenesses of the forms of almagda so that those who do not know them may see them, and they should be made of pure gold:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the heads of these be of this same subtlety, and the rear ones at three sharp angles.
de la char sor le neis	On the flesh next to the bone
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	There are times when different colored flesh joints appear on the bone. Some of these resemble scorpions with many feet, while others have flesh that is dyed red or flesh that is naturally soft-colored. You should place a patient with this soft-colored but not dyed flesh between your hands facing the sun, open their nostrils, and apply onion to those joints, rubbing them well. Then use a sharp, pointed scalpel on one side until you know that all of the flesh has been removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there is still something that cannot be scraped away, open it with one of the sharp instruments lightly and completely until nothing remains. And if without pain or heat, cover the wound with cotton, and if it is malignant sores, cauterize them quickly so that the blood stops flowing and all the flesh is removed. Then apply a poultice made of oatmeal and vinegar to the bone.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the bone opens and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is clean. But if moisture does not reach as it should, know that there is dead flesh on the bone above, so the instrument will not cut properly: therefore, you must insert a thread of soft linen, somewhat thick, and soaked in hot water with at least one grain of spice between each knot. The patient should place the head of the thread into their nostril with some force and inhale until it reaches the mouth. Children often do this at school, and it is an easy procedure for anyone who wishes to try it. Then hold the two ends of the thread in both hands, one at the nostril and the other at the mouth, and pull gently and steadily until you feel that the knots have reached the dead flesh. Continue this process until you know that the knots have rotted the flesh, then remove the thread, wipe away any blood, moisten it with Egyptian ointment, and reinsert it into the nostril as before. Repeat this procedure for three days or more until the ointment has destroyed all remaining flesh. Then place a plaster of lead over the nostril for several days until it is clean. If necessary, use drying medications. This is the method of using the instrument to purge the head, with which one distills oils and medications for the nostrils:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be made of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp with a tube like a candle wick, and the tube should also have many holes at its tip for purging the nostril; and if you wish to use a closed tube, make sure that the instrument is full of liquid for purging the head. And let it have several small openings at the top so that one can hold it securely while heating the oil or any other liquid.
de la char sor le neis	To cauterize flesh on the nostril:
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises at the head's top,
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the solution comes into one of these inflamed cartilages, it helps little, but some men. Therefore, when this happens to anyone, you should see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips together in a suture, and cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, you must scarify all the parts of their core until they heal, then join the two lips together in a suture, tighten them, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood and crushed incense on top. Then place a piece of strong plaster or other adhesive plaster on it, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is thus: either by needles, as we have said in the belly stitching; or by thread, as I have taught you.
des apostemes des levres	Chilblains on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many people have hard chilblains on the lips, resembling grains of wheat, small and large. Therefore, you should turn the lips and cut each nodule with scissors and remove it with tweezers by cutting in every part. Then apply powdered vitriol to the incision until the wound is clean. Afterward, wash the area with warm water and dress the wound with dry substances until it heals.
de la char des gencives	Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, attached flesh appears on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore, you should hold it with forceps and cut it at its root, allowing the blood vessel or vein to flow. Then apply powdered vitriol or other restrictive and drying powders to the area. If the flesh returns after the incision, which often happens, cut it again and cauterize it; afterwards, it will not return. These are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	Of boils
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, rough and sharp scabs appear on the gums in the mouth between the teeth, and sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, or worm-eaten, causing corruption to reach the gums and making the teeth smell bad. Therefore, you should have the patient sit with their head in your lap and raise their lips so that nothing remains on the teeth. Do this for blackness, greenishness, yellowness, and other stains until they are cleaned. If what caused it is removed at first, it is good; if not, resume cleaning on the second and third day until everything is clean. Know that teeth require various forms of instruments for cleaning according to what the work shows, as those used to scrape the outside of teeth have different shapes than those used to clean between them. Have all these forms and others ready with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you are treating a toothache, you should delay extracting it as much as possible, for this should never be done. For it is a very high and delicate substance until there is no other option but to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Therefore, when the patient is constrained to have a tooth extracted, you must be certain about the painful tooth. Often the pain may seem to come from one tooth while actually being in another, leading to the extraction of a healthy tooth, which we have often seen happen among these surgeons. Once you are sure about the painful tooth, cut around it with a strong and sharp scalpel to protect the gum tissue on all sides. Then use your fingers or forceps to gently pull the tooth back and forth until it is well loosened. Afterwards, firmly grasp the tooth with the forceps and have the patient sit with their head in your lap between your knees, ensuring they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth properly without breaking it, if it does not come out easily, use one of these instruments and gently insert it into each side of the tooth socket. Then move it back and forth as you did before. If the tooth is pierced or brittle, fill the hole with wool or cotton where it has broken. Then carefully grasp the tooth with forceps to extract it without breaking it. It is very important to work gently around the gum tissue to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Make sure not to break the tooth while extracting it, as leaving a piece behind can cause more severe pain for the patient due to the remaining root. Be careful not to act like ignorant surgeons who hurry and use force, sometimes breaking the jawbone or leaving parts of the tooth behind, leading to serious diseases from the remaining roots or broken bone, which we have often seen happen. After extracting the tooth, wash the socket with wine, vinegar, or salt water. If bleeding persists, apply powdered vitriol to the area. If this does not work, cauterize the wound.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments used for extracting teeth first should have long points and thick handles so they do not double over when pulling the tooth. These are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of large members so they do not bend when pulled, and of iron well-made, and toothed for moving them.
de la racine des dens	From the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains at the pull, then you must place on the spot cotton moistened with butter for one or two days until the spot is softened, then insert the tongs called "algefri", which seem like a bird's beak; and let them be made inside like a file; this is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with these tongs, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root, and put the tool called "althali", that is to say, pliers, this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with these, good; if not, then help yourself with all the tools, of which the shapes come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this tool with two handles, this is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments which are in front of the reason for teeth, and this tool that resembles large tongs, here is its shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let these tools be strong so they cannot break; and know that there are many instruments for teeth, and also others which are not counted. And the clever master finds his own instrument according to what his works and sickness show him, because there are such diseases where the old did not teach any instrument due to their diversity. And if one breaks something of the cartilage or other bones, then search among those tools which are necessary, as I have told you, and help yourself with gestures; this is its shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and hold well to hold the bone so it does not escape but can hold and remove it; then restore the place with appropriate medicine, and if there is rot in the bone and it is small, then remove it with all this tool.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear not according to the natural body shape and their appearance is ugly, especially in maiden women, it is necessary for you to know if the tooth is next to the tooth and not in the right place, and one cannot be set or smoothed: then cut; and if it is adherent with the tooth, take this tool of which here is its shape, resembling a small beak, and made of iron sharp at the end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And hit it gently day after day for the hardness of the tooth and so as not to move the others; and if it is apparent that one can smooth it, then use this kind of file, of which here is its shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and file the tooth gently day by day little by little so that it does not fall too much; then smooth it at the end with any rasp; and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then smooth its sharpness until it is even so that it neither hurts the tongue nor impairs speech.
quant li dent lochent	When teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When front teeth are loose, either by accident or falling, and the sick person cannot press on what they eat without it falling out, and you have treated them with tightening medicines but they don't help, then tighten them with a gold thread, for silver thread turns green and rots, but gold does not change. And let the thread be medium thickness neither too thick nor too thin according to the space between the teeth. If you see that the teeth can be aligned, take the thread and double-ended pliers between the two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the loose teeth, if there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side. Then start the wrapping again up to the point where you began, tightening your hand subtly and carefully so that it does not move. And let your binding be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the ends of the thread with pliers and bend them together between the healthy tooth, placing it so that it does not hurt the tongue. Then leave it tight as long as it can remain, and if it loosens or the thread breaks, then tighten it with another thread. Thus it will remain and serve for all its time; this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of the two healthy teeth and the two loose ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is replaced in its place little by little, as we have said; and let not those who are not wise and skilled meddle with it. And sometimes the shape of a cow's tooth bone is made and placed in the place where there is a gap, and it is tightened as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tie of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes this tie comes from under the tongue by nature or as a result of an injury wound. The operation is done thus: open the mouth of the sick person and have their head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous tie from above as much as needed so that the tongue is released from its attachment. If there is hardness or callus, which comes from a healed wound, use the point of a lancet to cut from above that tie. Be careful that the cut is not too deep lest you damage the artery below. When you have done this, wash the wound with rose water and sage, or cold water, then place a linen compress under the tongue; let the sick person keep it every night so that the wound does not heal over. If bleeding occurs, put powdered vitriol on the wound. If the blood continues to flow, cauterize it with a lentigo cautery, which is good for this purpose. Then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it with red or black color or hard and the sick person does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre. And if it tends to ooze pus, and there is moisture, use a lancet and carefully make an incision with a spatula, and deliver it on one side and the other. If blood flows from your operation, put powdered vitriol on it until it stops flowing, then return to your operation until you remove all furuncle. Then wash the wound with sage and celandine, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes there are lumps that appear in the throat which are called "godath", and they are properly called twin almonds. If these do not heal as we have described earlier, then be careful: if it is a hard abscess with dark color, do not touch it with an iron instrument. And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with an iron instrument either, especially to avoid bleeding. But let it ripen until it bursts by itself. If it is white and has a thin root, then prepare your instruments for cutting, but first make sure that the abscess is calm and relaxed. Then have the sick person sit facing the sun, with their head in your lap, and have them open their mouth wide and take hold of their tongue between their hands, pressing it down with all the instrument, which should look like this: it should be made of silver or thin brass, just like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue against all this instrument,
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, then take the forceps,
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be incised on one side and named on the other; and when you have cut one of the almonds, so cut the other according to the same manner, and afterward the patient should gargle with hot water and rue, and hyssop, and if blood flows, then the patient should gargle with water in which pomegranate peels or bay leaves have been cooked, and similar things, until the blood is stanched; then care must be taken until it is healed. And sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two almonds, so cut them then just like the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had grown inside her throat, namely one of small size. And it had almost entirely closed the throat so that the woman could not exhale because the passage was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she would have died if she had remained like this for one or two days. The abscess had grown so high that two needles had been placed through its nostrils. I therefore acted quickly and inserted a needle into one nostril, then withdrew it with some portion of bowel attached; afterwards I did the same on the other side of the nostrils and opened her mouth and pressed down her tongue. Then I inserted the needle into these abscesses and cut off part of them, from which only a little blood came out; thus the passage in the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, without ceasing to cut away at this abscess for a long time; and it grew back again, filling up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large. Then I drained it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it remained without growing further; and I left these parts, and I do not know what God did with her afterwards.
de l’uve	And when you wish to treat a man or woman whose eye is inflamed externally, take some of the powdered plant called "maiden's breath" (*Veronica officinalis*) and mix it with the yolk of an egg; apply this mixture around the eye on the eyelids. Then take a bandage made of linen and wrap it around the head so that it presses gently against the eye, but not too tightly. Leave the bandage in place for three days and nights without removing it to allow the patient to sleep comfortably. After three days, remove the bandage and wash the eye with warm water. Then apply some of the ointment made from rose oil mixed with wax to the eye, taking care not to get any of the mixture into the eye itself. Repeat this treatment for nine days, during which time the inflammation should decrease and the eye become healthy again.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the humor descends to the eye and it is inflamed and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; if it is beneath thick and rounded, it is called an "eye." When it is drained as we have said in its division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the hard tumor has subsided, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and that which is round and assembled and not elongated. And if it is sanguineous or of dark color or black, then you should avoid incising it. For there is great danger to the patient from this. Therefore, when you see it, according to its manner that I have said, of its inflammation and elongation, make the patient sit facing the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument mentioned before; then insert the awl into the eye humor, and draw it underneath, and cut it with one or two instruments mentioned in the incision of two mandibles. And you must not cut further than the natural limit; for if you cut more, it harms the voice and speech. And after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of two mandibles, and cure until it is healed.
