And if the patient fears the cutting, then you should use an instrument for cauterization of fear sense. The manner of cautery is acute hot water. It is that the patient puts his head in your hand, and then presses the tongue with the instrument mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and confined with boiling hot water, so it is not too thick nor too clear; and in employing this instrument, here is its form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And at the top there is a small hollow where one puts the medication, as if it were a spoonful of the medicine, and places the instrument entirely on the eye humor. And the patient should lie on his side so that saliva and mucus runs out of his mouth instead of the medicine entering the throat or the eye. Then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eye for about half an hour until you see it is darkened and the medication bites are apparent. And if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument entirely with the cotton into the canal above until the cotton touches the eye humor. Do this often until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry and fall off after four or five days. And if you need to restart the cauterization with medication, do so, and afterwards clean around the eye with cotton dipped in rose water, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water and cure with gargarisms until healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is better than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner: take calamint, hyssop, origanum, rue, chamomile, lavender and similar herbs, and assemble them all together in one pot. And add some of these herbs to the pot and let it boil well covered with thick earth. And there should be an iron instrument in the shape of a small spoon inside the pot:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it should be made of silver or bronze, and one of its ends is inserted into the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises up to the eye through the canal until the eye humor is mortified. Then begin again frequently until the eye is dried, but make sure not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot boil, because many things can happen; and do not do it before the decline of the hot boil. And if this instrument is not present, then take a pipe and put an eggshell at its end so that the mouth of the patient does not get too hot; for the eggshell does not let the vapor hurt the mouth, and this is good cure together.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times something sharp like a bone or fish spine, or any other thing gets stuck in the throat; so it is necessary that you remove what you can see and press the tongue with the instrument towards the sun until you see the object move. And what you cannot see but is stuck in the throat must be made to vomit by the patient before the food becomes cooked in the stomach; perhaps then the object will come out through vomiting. Or else the patient should swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a piece of lettuce root, or a small piece of dry bread; and tie one thread to the sponge, and then swallow it. And when it reaches the location, it will rise up, and then you can pull it out. And if it does not come out from what we have said, then take an instrument made of lead in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at its end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have its top lifted up. And make sure not to touch the epiglottis with it, nor push the bone too far in, but move the instrument gently until the patient feels where the object is stuck; then have them insert the instrument deeper or pull it out evenly until the object comes out completely.
de la sansue de la gorge	de la sansue de la gorge
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the cinder is cured without medicine, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines. And when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient towards the sun while pressing their tongue with the instrument that I have told you about. And if you see the cinder, then pull it out with a small pincer or with fine tweezers suitable for that purpose. And if this does not work, then take a hollow pipe and insert it into the patient's throat, then put a hot iron at the end of the pipe and do this frequently. And have the patient drink cold water all day long. Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, pour it in without swallowing, and move it with their hand frequently; as soon as the cinder feels the water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall out as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asphodel, using the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye. Do this many times, for it will come out without hurting them. And the manner of fumigation is this: take one pot with live coals in it, and cover its mouth with a pierced cloth in the middle, and put the end of the instrument into that hole. Then throw your fumigation onto the coals, and have the patient put the end of the tube into their mouth and close their mouth so that no smoke escapes but reaches the cinder; then the cinder will come out now, and if it does not fall out, then repeat the fumigation many times. And let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and sour things, and do not drink any water; then it will be necessary for it to come out by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which to treat the cinder is this: when it can be seen, it resembles curved tweezers for entering the throat. It should resemble a goose's bill and have sharpness like a file so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go. And here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	There are many kinds of abscesses, according to what is remembered here from one and the other in this book, and they are different in perforation and in size; and it is in two ways that the one is like itself, and those that contain moisture. And the second way is for the places where they are on the body, because the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of the fleshy place are different from those that come to the joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	"And therefore there are abscesses which one should not pierce until the bowels have died according to their fulfillment; and there are such as it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their fulfillment, such as abscesses that are near joints. For when an abscess comes near a joint, and it is left until it is putrefied all around, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb. Where the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the piercing until it has died, it will harm the principal member; where it is near the fundament, pierce it before it dies. And one should not pierce a ripe abscess without digestion being completed, except for those that are near the fundament, lest it perforate too deep and be elongated inside, and there come a fistula; and cannot heal in a long term."
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	"And you should know the hour of piercing an abscess that is dead according to its fulfillment, and that is when the pain has ceased, and the separation of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and from softening and hardness at the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should make the perforation where it depends more hanging down than the abscess, and where it opens most; and let the perforation be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and near nerves and arteries, and in all places smooth without fold."
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	"In those that are thick, according to that member. And when an abscess is in a hard place, it is better that you leave the piercing until it has solidified in complete digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before this time, then the body of the venom from it will be elongated, and it will be full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and the depth of it will harden. And there are some abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the members need. And you should make small incisions in small abscesses, small openings; and in large abscesses, large openings, and many splits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the heart, and cover: when it has become as large as a walnut, and has softened, then one should do like they do for boils: and there are such that are split into three angles, and there are those whose top is cut off like a fig leaf, like the abscesses of the armpits; and there are some where you make a round incision, and other incisions with similar cuts."
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Those that have no head, such as superficial soft abscesses, it is necessary that you pierce them plainly; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, then do not draw out all the pus at that hour, but draw out a part of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more of it again; do this several times little by little until all the pus is drawn out; especially if the patient is weak in strength, or pregnant woman, or small children, or old decrepit men. For the spirit sometimes jumps with the exit of the pus, which may suddenly kill the patient, and you would not notice it. Therefore, be careful in this chapter, and when you have pierced your abscess, then examine the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain cut, then prepare bandages of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then it is necessary that you put in each one a bandage so that they come together; and if you have cut off a piece of skin from the abscess, and have trimmed it around, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or lint without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed."
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if bleeding occurs from your incision, then prepare cold water and astringent, and moisten one cloth, and put it on the place where it is bleeding many times. And if the bleeding persists, if you apply compresses and treatment, and the powders that I have said in my hands in this book, and if it is in winter time, and the place where the abscess is very nervous, then it is necessary that you put on bandages and cloths moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer time, and the place is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put on bandages moistened in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; then remove the abscess and cleanse it and cure it, as it should be done, until it is healed."
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	"And this one must know universally in the cure of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the cure of abscesses, and here is this chapter."
des soros	"of sores"
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	"Abscesses of the head come from small abscesses, and they are kinds that we have in our skin, like the pores of a goose, and there are many similarities. There are some that are fatty and others that are moist like boils; and there are those that are hard and painful at the incision, and there is no doubt that the artery is against it. And the cure of the incision is this: you pierce with any instrument called 'entromissoire', of which the form comes hereafter, what thing it contains. For if it contains moisture, then cut through on top. And when the moisture is drained, then scrape without leaving anything of the skin that contains this moisture, because it returns again if one leaves something there; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and oil, and fill the wound, and leave it until the next day; and do the same on the second day and the third day, until you know well that nothing remains of the night; then cure the wound with appropriate ointment until it is healed. And if the abscess holds one fat boil, cut according to this form, long; and cast your onions there, and scrape from all sides, and put all your cure in drawing out the coat where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, then do what I told you after that. And do likewise for the abscess if it is painful, and of the cutting and curing as I have told you."
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	"And the incision on the painful and moist abscess is easier, because they contain little blood. And there are some of these abscesses on the head that have no moisture, and this was one of those abscesses that I cut out on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard, sharp, and white stone, and it could not be broken; and if one had struck any part of it, it would have made as much wound as a stone. And there are other kinds of abscesses that come on the head, except those that come on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be kept open for more mucus to come out; and cure them as they should."
des scrophules	Scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times these tumors occur on the neck, and under the armpits, and among the angles, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and they are many, and they are connected to each other. And each tumor is properly within its own side, like the boil and tumor of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these tumors are many. There are some that contain moisture, and there are some malignant ones that do not wish to obey health in this one then that you see with good appearance on touch, and is similar in color to the skin, and moves from every side and is not hard against the nerves of the neck nor the artery nor the duct, and is not deep; so it must be cut through above, and scraped from each part, and the two lips of the heart are opened at once if you need them, as we have said in boils of the head; and drain drop by drop, and make sure that you do not cut into the nerve or vein, and do not use an awl nor a knife that slips, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut into the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put crushed vitriol powder or some powders that stop bleeding in the wound, and constrain the wound; and leave it until the tumor is appeased, and the wound begins to soften and starts to decay. And when the blood is staunched, then return to your work until you have completed it; then examine with your index finger if there remain any small tumors, and cut them out and clean them up. And if there is a large vein at the root of the tumor, then it is not necessary for you to cut this tumor at its root, but tie it off with a double strong thread, and let it fall without harm; then fill the wound with cotton wool soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then dress it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut out the entire tumor, then you must join together the two lips of the wound and sew them up immediately, so that there is no excess left from the size of the tumor; then it is necessary to cut into the root of it, draw out pus, and sew it up as we have said. Those tumors that contain excess must be pierced where they appear most full; and pierce them in this manner as we have described before, taking care not to make too large an opening; then bring tents with ointment and similar things so that what remains may corrupt; and when the wound is well cleaned out, then dress it with warm ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	The term "squinance" does not appear to have a standard medical definition or usage in medieval or early modern surgical texts. It is possible that it was a regional or colloquial term used by surgeons of the time, but without more context, it is difficult to determine its meaning with certainty. If you can provide additional information about where this term appears and in what context, I may be able to provide a more accurate interpretation.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	This quote translates to: "The ancients spoke and discussed the operation of cutting for the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who performed it, and this is written in their words."
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who are strangling/choking, it is necessary that the opening of the throat called "epiglottis" be cleared away; and one should not offer assistance by this method because all the veins and the membranes of the patient are hot in the mouth or throat or in two lumens.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the vein, it is necessary to lift the epiglottis to avoid suffocation from choking.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four, through a small cut across between two circles or according to the quantity of the cut of the soft palate, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these circles are so close to the epiglottis that there is no flesh in between, and the vessels are long on either side.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is cautious, then he must extend the skin of the throat all along its length, and cut the heart as far as the chin; avoid the blood vessels if you see any, and then cut the soft palate as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe at the chin, which jumps forward when the circle that has been cut breaks, and by the loss of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour of doubt about strangulation has passed, bring together the two lips of the wound in the heart and sew it closed without including the cartilage; then apply medicines that promote healing until it is sound again.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely closed up, and the patient is judged to be near death, and the harm is done
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore, cut the epiglottis so that the patient can breathe again and avoid death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And therefore the ancients ordered that the wound be left open until the mischief of the disease has passed, and it passes in three or four days
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded that the wound be sewn up and healed, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young lady take a knife and stick it in her throat, cutting some of the tubes that carry air
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, but found her already dead
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	Upon examining the wound, I found that blood had flowed from it, and I knew for certain that she had not cut her veins or opened a passage through which air could escape, but that wind was escaping through the wound
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried and sewed up the wound and treated it until it healed
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And it happened to the young lady that she lost her voice temporarily, but afterwards returned to her usual state
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore I say that there is no fear in cutting the epiglottis
de la grosse gorge	of a thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This type of swelling is called "throat hernia," and it appears as a large, yellowish-colored tumor that occurs mostly in women
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and there are two kinds of it: natural, and accidental; or rather not having any cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And accidents occur in two ways: one resembles fat tumors, and the other resembles swellings that come from an artery
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear only in those cases which are small, and one should operate with caution on these alone, examining them thoroughly from within:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it as thick as one's thumb and not on any vein, cut it, as one cuts nails, and remove it completely if there is any.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And carefully check around the wound, and heal it properly until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	From us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many forms of us, all of which I will describe;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now it must be said what all the difference is between wound and dislocation
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is hot and has fever until boiling passes, and putrefaction is completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the knot there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains one siqac, which is its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a bag, becoming large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are according to two likenesses, either dry or moist, and many colors are as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of the knot, you must first examine and inquire with all the instruments called "trocar," according to what its shape will be as described in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring about the apostemes of knots is that you take the moistest part you find in the aposteme and turn your hands little by little until you know that the instrument has pierced the heart, then according to the size of the aposteme;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the trocar, and beware of what comes out of it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moist running blood occurs, whatever its color may be, lance it like I said for other apostemes;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	"If after the insertion the moisture does not come, know that it is thick, so cut it in cross and take it with forceps, and lightly scrape each side and guard the sheath where it lies so you draw it clean along with the knot."
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	"And if thou cannot draw it cleanly, then draw it in pieces so that nothing remains."
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	"For if anything remains, the moisture will return many times."
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	"And if some remains and the skin hurts you, then sprinkle the wound with some caustic waters, and bind it, and put on soothing plasters to draw out heat, and treat it with other treatments until it is clean."
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	"And if the moisture is great, then cut the two lips of the wound, and treat those that are near the flesh."
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	"And if the beating vein is against you or another, then hurry and apply the powder of vitriol ground, and let it lie for two or three days until the wound rots, and the ebullition of blood calms; then return to cut those that remain of the knot."
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	"Here are the shapes of insertion instruments, and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small. There are four squares called 'albarets' and one called 'breb', and there are also three kinds for encircling fistulas."
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	"And they are also like needles used for cutting ligatures, made of citrine brass or iron or silver. Those that are yellow are more valuable and are especially prized for encircling the curves of fistulas."
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	"And they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes."
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	"The shapes of forceps are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and there are also forceps with two curves in three sizes."
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	"And there are also forceps with three curves in three sizes; and those with two curves and single-curved forceps, all of which come in three sizes, and they are all necessary in their respective places."
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	"The tips of these are sharp for cutting, and there are some that only cut on one side, used to excise growths without damaging veins or nerves."
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	"And among these insertion instruments are the alemelles (small forceps) held in fingers, so that the patient does not perceive them at the opening of fistulas."
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	"And they come in three sizes: large, small, and medium, as you can see;"
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	"And these are only used in soft flesh areas, such as legs, arms, breasts, angles, and similar places;"
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	"Sometimes another small instrument is used, resembling forceps, according to this shape, with which blood is wiped away:"
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	"And it is sometimes placed at the site where there is danger of cutting veins and arteries, and sometimes they are large in size:"
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	"Sometimes the breasts of certain men become inflamed when they begin to be corrupted, so that they appear like those of a woman;"
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	"And they remain unsightly and inflamed; whoever wants to treat them must follow this shape, from line B to G:"
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	"Then excise the fat, fill the wound with healing ointment, then approximate the two lips of the wound to suture, and heal it until it is sound;"
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	"If the breast hangs down and is soft due to its size, like those of women, then it should be cut in two parts above, through two similar incisions;"
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	"So that one part holds the other at the end of each, such that the larger part contains the smaller according to this shape, from line B to G;"
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	"Then excise the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about suturing and powders, and whatever is necessary for healing until it is sound;"
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	"And if it is not healed or the incision is not complete because the patient will not rest or due to bleeding, you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive ointment;"
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	"And leave it until it consumes the remaining flesh and fat, then heal it until it is sound."
des apostemes des asselles	Of armpit fistulas
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	"These fistulas that come under the armpits are of the type of hard scrofula with lumps, and some contain moisture."
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	"Therefore, those that contain moisture must be cut according to this shape, from line B to G:"
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when the entire lump in the fistula has been emptied, fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and heal it with appropriate ointment until it is sound."
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	"And if the fistula resembles scrofula, cut it like we have said for scrofula incisions; and if the wound gapes open, apply a caustic as we have mentioned before."
de la routure de l’artere	Of arterial rupture
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	"When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it adheres, fistulas often form, and the same happens with an enlarged vein and fistula;"
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	"And if one recognizes this when it is due to the artery, then the fistula will be long and deep;"
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	"And when you feel it with your fingers, you sense an instrument; and when it is due to the vein, it appears clearly inflamed;"
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	"It is foolish to cut this fistula, especially when it is under the armpits and angles, at the neck, and in many other places where it is very large;"
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	"Therefore, the cure of iron should be avoided, and the one at the head should also be avoided; and in that which is due to arterial inflammation, cut through the skin above it lengthwise;"
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	"Then make an incision along its length, carefully separating the artery from the tissues until it is exposed;"
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	"Then place a needle beneath it and pierce it through to the other side, and tie the artery with a doubled thread in two places, as I have taught you regarding the extraction of the two arteries located in the temples;"
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	"Then place the site between the two ties with an introjector until the blood stops flowing there, and the fistula should be drained;"
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	"Then apply healing ointment to fill up the hollow until the tie falls off;"
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	"Then heal it with appropriate ointment until it is sound;"
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	"And if the fistula is due to an incision of the vein, you should stretch your hand over everything from the fistula to the skin,"
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	"Then place the needle beneath the site you are holding with your hand, pierce it through to the other side, and pass one doubled thread through it;"
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	"Then tie the fistula as I have told you, with the ligature of one of its two ends to both ends of the thread;"
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	"And if you doubt that the son may not pierce, insert another needle at the base of each thread below all the abscess to the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places."
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	"Then cut the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut away the excess from around the heart and leave what is tied."
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Then place a cloth dampened in wine and oil on top, then apply dressings and poultices until it is healed."
des apostemes des ners	"Abscesses of the nerves"
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, abscesses can come to the artery and vein, abscesses also come to the nerves when they are injured or from excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	"And this happens more often at the joints and fingers, especially in places where there are joints, and it is a serious abscess that appears similar to the skin's color but has various sensations without pain."
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	"And when it is tightly bound, the sick person feels pain, and it is not deep in the body but underneath the heart;"
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	"And it moves well from all sides and does not spread forward or backward, up or down, and an abscess in the joints should not be cut with iron: it might cause contraction."
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	"And those that are on the head or forehead are pierced with a scalpel."
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	"If the abscess is small, grasp it with tweezers and cut it at its root;"
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if it is large, suspend it with the forceps, scrape it off, then cut and sew up the wound, and apply dressings until it heals."
des grosses boces pendans	"Hanging boil sores"
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	"Sometimes it occurs in the belly and nowhere else, and it is called 'funge' due to its appearance. The root is subtle while the head is large; there are both small and very large ones."
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	"And I saw one man who had two on his belly that resembled funguses more than anything else, with no difference between them. They were white and had a thin root, they were already split open, and there was always moisture coming out."
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	"I cut them open and found that one weighed eighteen ounces and the other six. The contents of the incision were moist, with white, moist flesh and a thin root."
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	"So cut it open with a wide scalpel and have hot cautery ready nearby. For at the incision there often comes too much bleeding, and if blood flows abundantly, then quickly apply cautery."
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	"And if you see the patient trembling and afraid of the scalpel incision, take a well-made thread of flax and tie it around the abscess as we have said, leaving it on for two days;"
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	"Then tighten it and continue to pull on the flax thread until the abscess opens, without any effort. If the roots are large, be afraid of cutting them near the belly, but you can still cut half of it."
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	"Then cauterize it so that it does not return. Then dress the wound and make sure not to cut into the boil that is of dark color, poor sensation, and milky secretion."
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	"For this is an enchanted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of cancer later on."
quant li boude ist fuer	"When the boil bursts"
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	"If the boil appears due to cautery of a wound or tear of the anus, and is on the belly where some boils occur as with other eruptions, or from blood flowing from veins or arteries, or from windiness;"
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	"Or if it is from the rupture of the anus and the outlet of the bowel, then the boil's color resembles that of flesh. It causes little pain or sensation, and has various outlets."
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	"And if it is due to the outlet of the intestines, then it appears more diverse. When pressed between two fingers, it pops up and then returns. Sometimes it is hard, and grows larger at the entrance of the anus with great effort."
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	"And if it is due to moisture, it appears easily and opens well when pressed with the hand, without constriction. But if it is due to blood, then the boil appears large and hard, fixed in place according to its quantity;"
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	"And if it is due to windiness, it feels soft to the touch. The contents appear as you observe whether it is from arterial or venous blood, or windiness."
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	"So you should leave the treatment alone for now, as there is doubt and fear regarding both artery and vein, as I have mentioned in the chapter on boils."
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	"And if the appearance is due to the intestines or the bowel, then you should tell the patient to lie down with their arms extended and knees bent, surrounding the boil with pressure;"
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	"Then place your hands on either side of the boil."
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	"Then go around where you have marked off with the scalpel."
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	"Then stretch half of the boil upwards, using your thumb and index finger."
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	"Then tie it firmly with a strong thread or silk cord, making sure that the knot is secure."
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	"Then open the stretched half of the boil above the ligature and insert your thumb and index finger to find the intestines;"
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	"If you find it trapped by the ligature, untie it and place the intestine back inside the belly."
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	"If you find the bowel, grasp it with your thumb and index finger and cut off any excess;"
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	"And if the artery or vein opposes you, carefully go around it, then return to your task and take two needles, insert them through two strong threads, and cross them where you pierced."
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	"Then squeeze the boil in four places above the needles and remove them if necessary, leaving the ligature until it rots and the dead flesh falls off."
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	"Or cut it when it becomes soft and rotted, then dress it as necessary, and remove the boil as we have said."
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	"And remove any blood or moisture you find, then dress the wound as necessary and close it with stitches."
dou chancre	"Regarding cancer"
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	"We have discussed the appearance of cancer and how to treat it with medications in our division. We must also be cautious when treating cancerous ulcers in the marrow or large ones that are difficult to excise, such as those found in the breast, thigh, and similar locations. The ancients advised removing them completely when they first appear, but once they become large and old, it is not advisable to approach them as I have never seen anyone cured of cancer, nor has anyone else before me."
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when the cancer is located in an area where it can be removed, as we have said, you should purge the patient with black bile once or twice. Then let him fast if he shows signs of repletion. Next, prepare a good operating site to perform the surgery. Then grasp the cancer with your thumb and index finger, cut it off from all sides, and remove it completely without leaving anything behind. Allow the blood to flow freely, wipe the wound clean with your hand or any other object, and if bleeding from the incision of an artery or vein opposes you, cauterize it until the bleeding stops. Then treat the wound with other remedies until it is healed."
de ydropisie	Dropsey
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have previously discussed in the chapter on dropsy its similarities and how the accumulation of water is formed, as well as the signs of each similarity, and the treatment that is done with medicines, and that which is treated with iron: only this is selected; and one should not touch iron in these two semblances: namely tympanites and hypospadias, for it is deadly. Therefore, when you treat this dropsy semblance called "eclites" with medicine and the treatment does not help, see if the patient is weak or if they have another disease besides dropsy, such as thirst and abdominal swelling etc.; do not touch iron, there is doubt; and if you see that the patient has great strength and they have no other disease but dropsy alone, and they are not too young nor too old, then you should operate thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Raise the patient upright onto your hands, and have the assistant press the abdomen while forcing water out of the lowest part of the chest. Then take a spatula with a sharp, pointed blade, about two inches wide but not so sharp that it can reach the intestines when inserted, nor able to cause bleeding;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	then look if dropsy has entered towards the intestines: then it is necessary that you cut .iii. fingers breadth above on the right side of the wrist; and if dropsy is due to liver disease, then your cut should be on the left side of the wrist .iii. fingers breadth; and if it's due to mucus, then it should be on the right, and it is not necessary that the patient lies on the cut so that excesses do not run to that weak place
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	then pierce all the skin with the instrument and remove it, then raise your hand to the entire spatula between the skin and the syfac as when scraping by the quantity of one nail or around it; then pierce the syfac until the spatula reaches the empty place, and that is the location of the water, then draw out this instrument, which has this shape: And it resembles a thin silver pipe, and it is made of copper or lightweight brass, and at its lower part there is one small hole; and on one side there are three holes, and two on another side, and one on another; and the blade is cut like a pen, and that is the shape of the incision with which writers cut pens
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top of it is the alembic, so that when the instrument reaches the water, then tilt it up; then empty one-third or half of it, for if you pour out more than necessary at this time, by chance the patient may die from the spirit's resolution leaving the weapon, or he may faint or approach death
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to its quantity and according to what the dispositions of the sick person's virtue indicate and his pulse; then draw out the instrument and retain the water, which is now retained by the heart that stops up the hole that is on the syfac, about which I have spoken, which you pierce in this manner; then begin the instrument again on another day if you see the patient enduring these things, and draw out a small quantity of water
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	do this for a few days, and be careful not to draw out too much water at once. And if you doubt about the patient, and leave him with too much water, then cure him with hot ashes or sand, and often bathe him in sweat and sun, and let him drink; and give him drying medicines until he is sound, and cauterize on the stomach and liver and spleen after extracting the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stoppage of the wand
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Sometimes children are born without any hole in the penis, or with a small one, or one that is not in its proper place. Then it must be pierced as soon as possible with a very thin spatula according to this shape: then put a thin leaden plug into the hole and tie it and hold it for three or four days, and when he wants to make urine, remove the plug and let him urinate, and then replace it; but sometimes there is no need, because the urine that comes out will not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose hole is small are medicined with the lead plug, as we have said, and it will widen. Those who do not have the hole in its proper place are crippled, because some are born with the hole at the tip of the penis, for which they cannot urinate until they lift their penis up; and they cannot enter because the matter cannot reach the opening, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of performing the operation is that the patient lies on his back, then stretch out the head of the penis and cut it off like the shape of a pen's nib so that the hole falls in the middle as it should; but be careful not to cut too much, because many times blood comes out, and if this happens, then stanch the blood with whatever stops bleeding, and cure the wound until it is sound.
des pustules de la verge	of the sores of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these albatrosses appear on the member, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; and there are malignant ones and non-malignant ones; so you must take them with a subtle pincer, cut and clean all, then place moistened cotton in Egyptian ointment; then treat with diaphoretic ointment until it heals.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the albatross is malignant, of foul color and foul-smelling, you must bring cautery to it. When you have cut it out, and if the albatross is in the very top of the member, and has part inside the skin and part outside, you must first remove the albatross that is inside; and when it is removed, then treat what remains outside. For when you treat them together, the flesh of the member may not be sure not to be pierced, and blackness and corruption come in the member and on the joint; so you must cut away all that is black and corrupted, then bind up the place with honey and flour made from the rind of pomegranates and figs, then treat it with other cures until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if there is profuse bleeding, bring the lunar cautery according to this form: This cautery helps with two dispositions together: namely, for profuse bleeding and corruption; and if the flesh of the member is corrupted and retracted, you must place a lead pipe on the end of the member and have the sick person piss through it; and when the skin at the head of the member is tough, which happens in those who have not been circumcised, or where there is wound or aposteme, then you must burn it with one heated instrument until the ties are loosened, and the flesh of the member is delivered from all sides;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	"And if it is difficult to separate these, then you must cauterize with one spatumile of hot water from the head of the penis and the skin; then carefully open between two fingers, and place one thin linen cloth moistened in cold water so that it may not burn again."
de la circoncision	"of circumcision"
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	"Circumcision is not a continuous dismemberment like other wounds; nonetheless, when we perform this operation willingly and properly on children, it is necessary to make the best and easiest work for salvation."
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	"I say that the ancients did not circumcise their children, for it was not used in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience."
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	"Because I have seen most masters and senior surgeons performing circumcision with only one dal, without forceps, and using just one novacula; thus it happened that the skin remained torn because there were two layers, and sometimes they cut the upper one and leave the lower one."
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.
