"Otherwise, they cut it again, and the pain is doubled; moreover, at the time of cleansing the wound from the dal, the point of the member is not securely protected; also, during cleansing of the nail, sometimes the iron slips and damages the work, and many times it happens that there is no need for cleansing, which I have seen."
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	"Concerning the cleansing that is done with forceps and with the entire length of thread, I have found through experience its goodness because the forceps cuts evenly both above and below."
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	"But when you press your hand, it cuts equally in just one single moment; but be sure that the thread is tightly wrapped around the skin. Also, during the first operation, make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the penis and then make him laugh in every way you can."
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	"Then make the child sit upright between your hands, and put the forceps behind your back or under your feet so that the child does not see them nor any of the instruments. Then place your hand on the penis and blow onto the heart, and pull it upwards until the skin of the penis is stretched. Then cleanse it well from the dirt gathered there, then tie a double knot with a thread around the foreskin, then tie another knot underneath the first one. Hold the penis with your two fingers at the second knot near the pouch and the index finger, and cut between the two knots, then quickly lift the skin upwards and pull the head of the penis."
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Then let the blood flow little by little because it is beneficial; then put powder on top and cover the powder with a bandage glued with a half of a cooked egg yolk, tempered with rose water, mixed with good fresh rose oil. Leave it on until the next day, and dress it again until it is healed."
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	"The shape of the forceps for cleansing should be like this: the two jaws should be thin and sharp, and the jaws should be as large as the middle finger, evenly."
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	"The error in cleansing is when the skin inside is stuck to the incision; therefore, it is necessary that you stretch it with your fingernail before the edges stick together and cut it evenly. And if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with forceps and cut it."
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	"And if it has passed three days and the skin underneath the penis is swollen, let it be until the inflammation is calmed down, then carefully scrape it off; cut as much as you can without damaging the penis itself."
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Then treat the wound with powder for sudden wounds, as we have mentioned in our treatment of powders. And if you cut too much from the skin and it goes upwards, it will not harm at all. Then treat it as we have said until it is healed."
dou retenement de l’urine	"Regarding the retention of urine"
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is caused by the obstruction of a stone, or frozen blood, or a bowel, or flesh born there, or similar things, as we have said in the section on divisions.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	If the urine is not released and you see that it is retained because of a stone located in or near the neck of the bladder, then the patient should be made to sit on his heels. His feet should be placed on his back and he should extend his belly towards where his back meets his thighs, holding himself up as much as possible. This will cause the neck of the bladder to be pressed upwards, forcing the stone out so that urine may flow freely again;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	"And if it doesn't come as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called 'syringe', of which this is the form: and let it be of thin, light silver, like a bird's feather; and let its cane be one-and-a-half palms long, and let it be sharp at the head."
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	"And the manner of issuing urine is thus: take one doubled thread, and tie at its head a pouch of wool or cotton, and put the thread's head inside the syringe; then cut off the excess wool and put it up to the syringe's head, then oil the syringe with olive oil or butter from an egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a seat, raise their bladder and penis with moistened warm water and olive oil,
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	"then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then fold the penis upwards towards the belly; then push the syringe forwards until it reaches the bladder, and the patient feels the emptiness approaching, and if this is not done according to this order, it may be because the channel through which it goes is twisted. Then pull out the thread with all the wool pouch and pouch, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it and let the urine flow."
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	"And continue with the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and then relieve the patient."
des maladies de la vessie	Maladies de la vessie
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	"If blood or pus comes into the bladder, or if there is putrefaction gathered there, and you see that water and medicines are being distilled, then use all the instrument called 'clasp', and this is its form:"
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	"It is closed at one end, and has three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you can see. The place where the medicine comes out should be so narrow that it fits tightly around the penis without any addition, so that moisture can be drawn out and medicine inserted when necessary."
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	"And when you see that your medicines are being discharged into the bladder, put the end of the catheter into the moisture and draw out what is inside it. Then draw back the catheter strongly, so that the moisture enters and reaches the bladder, so that the patient feels it."
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	"And this is the form of the subtle catheter used to catheterize the bladder:"
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	"And it is made of silver or brass, and the top part is higher. Below there are two breasts where the ligature falls. Then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the moisture with which you wish to catheterize the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts formed by a doubled thread, and heat one pouch of this moisture over the fire. Then insert the end of the catheter into the penis, and press your hand on the bladder until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder;"
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	"And if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment and make a circle from it, and pierce it roundly all around. Then put a strong thread through these holes, then close the circle like a hat, and put inside what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument. And do as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder."
de la piere	"de la pierre"
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	"We have previously stated in the division the methods of stone, and their extraction together with medicines; and I have mentioned the difference between stone lodged near the kidneys, and all its signs, and in which stone one must operate by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you this clearly and briefly."
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	"I say that stone which is lodged in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder appearing like water in its subtlety; and it makes the patient's penis appear harenaeous, and he feels great pain and frequently urinates, and then stiffens; and many of these cases have a foundation; and the healing of children is easy until they are four years old, and it is very difficult for the elderly, and it is moderate for youths, for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one."
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	"And when it comes to the cure, first we must cleanse the patient by using an enema to remove all the feces that are in the intestines. For they sometimes hinder searching for the stone."
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	"Then take the patient by their feet and raise them up and move them downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and it sometimes falls from its high place; then make him sit between your thighs with his hands underneath his thighs so that the bladder is completely inclined downward; then feel for it and touch it inside."
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut upon the stone. And if it does not fall at the touch of all, then moisten your left-hand index finger with oil, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is a full-grown youth; and insert it into its base, and seek the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, then wrap it around the neck of the bladder; then press down on your finger, and throw it out through where you saw to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and he commands that he stretch out his right hand upwards and remove the skin that is below the thighs in the part where the cut is made, then insert the spatula thus shaped.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make an incision between that which is between the thighs and the fundament, not in the middle but on the side of the left buttock; and let it be straight across the stone, and your two hands should always be at the fundament, and the cut should be wide at its opening and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	If by chance the pressure of your hands on the fundament causes it to spring forth without labor; and know that there are stones that have angles and edges: these are difficult to extract; but there are also those that are smooth and round like a bead, whose extraction is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	Therefore for those stones that have angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, then you must extract it with forceps that are also shaped like a file at the end, to hold more tightly so that the stone does not escape; or insert underneath one subtle instrument curved at the end; and if you cannot grasp it thus, then enlarge the hole a little bit, and if the skin is torn, then compress it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there is more than one stone, then first insert the largest one into the neck of the bladder, then cut above it, then draw it out, and then the smaller ones afterwards if there are many. And if it is very large, then it must be so, and make a larger wound. For two things can happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes forth continually from where the flesh cannot heal; but nevertheless strive to extract it, or crush it with forceps, until you draw it out in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, then fill the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and compress it, and place upon it a wet cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to cool the hot inflammation; then bind up the patient tightly around his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you untie him, then wash the wound very well with oil and water, then apply the ointment of diacynthion and the ointment of basilicum until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if hot inflammation and corrosion come into the wound, and congealed blood collects in the bladder, and urine is retained by this means so that it does not flow out with urine: then insert your finger into the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains there it will corrupt the bladder and cause it to decay.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then wash the wound with water and salt and oil, and help him in every way that you know until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the hours that you care for him, you bind his two thighs together, and gather the medicines upon the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small and it lies in the passage of the penis and has become fixed there so that urine cannot come out; then care for him as I have said before, except you should not cut him repeatedly, or excuse yourself from cutting with this cure. I have already proven this method thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron awl shaped thus and having three prongs forged into one stake:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take one thread and bind it around the stalk beneath the stone so that it cannot retreat into the bladder; then insert the probe lightly into the stalk until it reaches the stone; and rotate the probe in your hand against the stone little by little until you can pierce the stone from the other side; then urine will soon come forth, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the stalk. Thus it is quickly broken, and it flies out with the urine, and the patient is cured.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this because of something that prevents it, then tie one thread under the stone and another above, then insert the wand against the stone between the two threads, then pull it out forcefully, and untie the knot, and cleanse the wound from the congealed blood that is in it; and dress it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Of women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stones are dislocated in women's cases, and if it happens sometimes, its treatment is difficult, and it is forbidden for three reasons: the first one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second one is that one cannot find a knowledgeable woman who exposes herself to doctors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a knowledgeable woman in this art of healing; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more deeply placed than the stone of man, for which reason it requires a deeper cut, and there is great fear involved.

En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	I never saw anyone in this region who dared to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is done in the same way as the procedure seen above, so that you bind the vessels together after cutting them slightly above and then lightly below.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cut it in half, and drain the boil of the person who is working until the vessels bleed out, and then treat it as we have said until it is healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	There will never be an opening between the angles as we have said, and the location opens up without any intestines protruding from it. If any do protrude, it is only a little bit, and they are repaired immediately.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	And even if it remains too long in this state, the wound becomes infected or gangrenous to the extent that the intestines protrude.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	And this happens due to the extension of the gangrene which is at the angles, as we have said. This causes the area around it to soften and swell up, opening it further.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	And this condition is treated by cautery, as we have said before, but there are cases where it is not treated with iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and that the patient lies often on their back between your hands and then cut off the inflamed area around the wound with a knife to a depth of about three fingers.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	Then remove the gangrene that is under the skin and take some hot iron and place it on the exposed area of the gangrene.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	Then press the hot iron firmly against the depth of the abdomen, then sew up the two exposed surfaces of the gangrene onto the top of the iron and sew them together individually.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then remove the head of the iron, and do not cut off any gangrene or extend the wound in any other way, as I have explained to you regarding the treatment of an intestinal hernia.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then treat it according to the treatment of wounds. And when you cut the sutures, cleanse and dress the wound until it is healthy.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	Gangrene is contained and does not show itself in the wound, and cauterization is muted in this area, being closer to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	due to softening of the skin around the anus
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin around the anus in some men becomes softened because the tissues inside are softened, and it is unpleasant to see. And when you want to treat it, make the patient lie on their back and cut away the softened skin from the natural skin. Then bring the two lips together with one stitch and if necessary, sew the excess softened skin at three or four places firmly. Then cut between the stitches and treat it like other wounds until it is healthy, and remove the sutures.
dou chastrement	of castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and it would please me not to speak of it in this book. However, there are two reasons why it may be necessary: one is for the physician to respond when asked about it and know how to perform it, and the other is because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, dogs, and other beasts. I say therefore that castration is performed in two ways: either by traction or by cutting. In the method we use traction, make the animal sit in warm water until the testicles are softened and pendulous, then grasp them with your hand so they are relaxed and you no longer feel them. For castration by cutting: tie up the animal and press the skin around the scrotum with your left hand, then cut each testicle with one stroke after you have carefully peeled it. Leave some of the gangrene attached and remove the thin layer of skin on the vessels; this method is gentler than that done by traction because sometimes something may remain of the testicles, causing the animal to desire lust. Then treat the wound until it is healthy.
des hermofrodites	on Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphroditism occurs in two ways among men: one way is that between the two testicles there opens a figure like that of a woman's nature, with hair and sometimes urine flows through it. The other way is in women who have both a clitoris and two testicles on their pubic area. The treatment for both men and women is to cut away all the excess tissues and treat them like other wounds. However, there is no cure for those men whose urine flows through the skin of the scrotum.
de la tentigene	of tentingene (i.e., tentingene)
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Tentigene is a growth attached to the natural part,
de erratique	erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	Erratical is when the nature of woman is not clear, or the opening is small; and it is either born that way or caused by illness, or caused by excess flesh attached to it. It prevents conception, childbirth, and sometimes menstruation; recognition of this condition can be made by examining the vagina. If the obstruction is close to the entrance, then it will be near your two fingers or thumb. If it is due to excessive flesh, and it is close to two fingers, then quickly act accordingly: put your two index fingers together and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then stretch your two fingers open until the excess flesh covers the obstruction. Then take wool soaked in oil and place it on the site, and keep the woman lying down each day so that it does not close up. And if the obstruction is hard and thick, you must use a scalpel similar to a laurel leaf shape. If the obstruction is born from flesh, then scrape it off with a spoon and cut it open; have medicines that stop bleeding ready, such as aloe, dragon's blood, incense mixed with egg yolk. Then apply a wide bandage so that the wound does not close up, and continue to do this for a long time until there is a dry linen dressing; then treat with other remedies until it is healed. And when flesh grows in the uterus, you must cut according to this method if it is not an infected ulcer. Because one should not touch a charmed ulcer that is in the uterus out of fear.
des emorroides	"For hemorrhoids"
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	**Translation:**
des apostemes de la marris	Of boils of the belly
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many types of boils occur in the buttocks, such as cancer and pearly boils and herpes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot boils, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division. Therefore it is necessary for me to speak in this treatise about the hot boil that occurs in the buttocks, which is not one of those boils that grow on the skin; and if you want to know how to treat it, look to see whether the boil is growing at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and becomes red if you can see it. Therefore do not rush to pierce it, but let it grow until the pain has subsided; and then make the patient sit on one seat, and have two small seats where they can lie down, and support their back and bring their feet together towards the thigh; and spread their thighs apart, and put their arms under their knees, and tie them tightly with a good knot; then suck out the contents towards the right side, and prepare the instrument for opening the mouth of the buttocks, about which more will be said below; and it is necessary that when you are preparing this instrument, you first insert the trocar to know the depth of the buttocks so that what goes inside does not go too deep and wound the patient; and if the instrument is too large, it is necessary to cover the depth of the buttocks with cloths so that the instrument does not hurt them; and it is necessary that you put the funnel of the instrument on top and moisten the instrument. And when the boil opens, and you open it gently by hand, then you must cover its head with a spatula made of lead; and when the bowel is emptied, it is necessary to put moistened tents in rose oil or dry green oil into the wound, and put the tent at the bottom of the buttocks and put some on top of the buttocks and on the linen cloth moistened with water where mallows have been cooked; then afterwards treat it for two days with appropriate ointment until it is healed; and sometimes you can raise the buttocks and the wound by a clyster of water and honey, and then with water in which roots of lily and long aristology have been cooked; then return to the ointment. And if the wound has closed inside the buttocks, then you must guard against cooking with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	The midwife's duty is first to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing downwards and wanting to smell the air; then the child hastens to come out. Know that this kind of birth is according to nature, and the afterbirth is with its head, and the waters with it; and when you see these signs, then press her belly lightly so that the child comes out quickly; for when it settles on its head, then the afterbirth is with it, and the mother's womb is cleansed of its superfluities by good cleansing. And those that come otherwise do not come naturally; for sometimes they come on their feet, and the body or buttocks come forth first, and the hands, or they come on their belly, or sometimes, and are turned by chance over their neck, and in other evil figures; therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should assist her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out naturally on its head and the woman is giving birth with difficulty, and her strength is weak, then let her sit on a stool or have women hold her up; and let the nature of oil or fenugreek be cooked, and then put the little spatumile between her thighs, of which this is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and break the afterbirth, and cut with your nail so much that the moisture inside comes out; and press on the woman's belly until the child comes down, and if it does not come down, then let her be purged with a mixture of fenugreek and sesame oil. Then let her sneeze and blow her nose with condici, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come out. And if the two hands come out first, you must gently squeeze them little by little; and if they cannot be put back in, then let the woman sit on a chair, and lift her feet up high; then knock the chair down to the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall with the chair. And if the hands cannot be put back in, and the child dies, then cut off the hands at the wrist with the knife placed beforehand, and pull out the child, and squeeze it evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	Of the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes out on its feet,
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn him gently bit by bit until he is even
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	then take one of his feet and extend it gently bit by bit
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	If he can jump up to the thighs, then command him to grasp it, and let him sneeze accordingly.
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	if by chance he jumps, God willing
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he does not jump as we have said, then turn him bit by bit until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easy
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if he does not come as we have said, then take myrrh, oil of sesame, and molten gum, and grind them all together in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	and place the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment

puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a seat, then make her sneeze and press her mouth and nose, and gently take hold of her belly, for the child will jump now
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	place the exit of the child upon her knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the child comes in this manner, then the midwife should place her hands bit by bit

de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the exit of the child that comes from the side with one hand hanging
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	I must devise how to bring back the hand
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman rise up and go away

de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the exit of the child upon her neck, with its hands spread out and its face turned towards its mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	the midwife must take hold of her hand, then turn it little by little, and gently bring forth the child

de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same manner for all that remains of the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes forth in this manner with all the afterbirth, then cut the afterbirth at your nail until the moisture is emptied
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	and if the child is hanging by its face and neck, then cut from the chin so that it may not be retained, and thus the child will die
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then place the child inside until you have put it in as it ought to be, and command the woman to press down once more
adonques si istra legierement.	then it will be drawn out easily
de l’issue des gemelz	about the exit of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are often born, and sometimes even three or four; this is not a rare thing, and it happens infrequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two [twins] are strange things, and they do not live long unless named
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that when they are multiplied, they are divided by the sac which separates them, which is attached to the chin
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they come out as naturally as one alone, just as we have said
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they cry out loudly when they come forth, then care for them as we have said, and let the midwife be skilled and do quickly and easily what she does
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do thus as it befits to preserve health
de plusors enfans	about several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes they are formed in the mother's womb one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or even more up to fifteen, and all of them are perfectly formed like a child according to the measurement of the holy spirit
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and the midwife must know all these things because sometimes such thing happens accidentally;
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	so she should do what is necessary
de l’enfant mort	about a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you care for the woman with a dead child in her womb, as I have said in the previous section, and it does not come forth, and you are compelled by duty to use your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	then you must know if the woman is of good health, and has no accident or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	then it is necessary for the woman to be laid on her back with her hips inclined downwards, and her legs raised up;
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	and the priest takes hold of two parts of her body or binds her to the bed so that she may not be moved during the delivery of the child;
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oil mixed with myrrh, aloe, fenugreek and linseed, then the midwife anoints her hands with these oils and myrrhs;
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	then insert her hands gently into the womb, then turn them once or twice where she has inserted them that they may be convenient for this purpose;
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take care that the child is properly arranged so that it comes out with its head downwards;
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	then fix the hooks into its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or in the navel or near the ribs;
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	and if the delivery is by feet first, then fix the hooks to the hips and at the middle of the sides;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	and it is necessary that she takes the hook with her right hand and places the curved part between her left elbow, and gently inserts her whole hand into the womb and fixes the hook in one of those places we have mentioned until it reaches its purpose;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the hook:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then fix another hook opposite the first one, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction may be equal on both sides;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then draw them out equally by moving one side and the other, to make it come forth, and let the hooks be toothed to hold it, as this is the shape:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	"And if a part remains, let him smear some of his own dung on two fingers, place them in that part, and draw out the other part."
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	"And if nothing remains, then place this poultice even higher up and do so until it all comes out."
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	"And if one hand comes before the other and he cannot bring it back due to tightness,"
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	"then you must wrap a cloth around it until it all comes out;"
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	"Then cut into the joint of the sole or on the side, and you must do the same to the other hand, having two feet."
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	"And if the child's leg is swollen and it is tight at the exit, or there is a sharp point assembled at its head,"
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	"then you must insert the spine of the swordfish between your fingers and cut off the head and remove the bone."
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	"or you could saw it with the instrument called 'almidach', from which the form comes, along with the tools listed in the chapter that follows this one;"
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	"And do the same if the child naturally has a large head;"
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	"and then pull out the bones like tweezers,"
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	"And if the leg jumps out and it is stuck in place, cut until the moisture at the exit of the wound comes out;"
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	"If it still cannot come out, then cut it into pieces with a saw that you have."
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	"And if it is swollen in the belly or below the ribs, you must pierce it until the moisture flows out."
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	"If the child is standing on its feet and the attraction is light, and the direction towards the mouth of the womb is easy,"
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a .i. drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	"And if it is tight in the belly or the wound, you must pull it out with one hand wrapped in a cloth."
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	"and cut into the belly or the wound until the moisture flows out;"
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	"And if the other limbs are disjointed and the leg remains,"
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	"then insert your hand deep into the womb and pull it up to the mouth of the womb;"
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	"then insert one or two fingers, and pull it out."
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	"And if the mouth of the womb is narrowed because of a hot boil that has come there, then one should not operate,"
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	"but rather apply moist and fatty things."
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	"And the plaster should be made from softened and moistening ingredients."
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	"And if the child is on its side and you can place it flat, then apply what we have said for a living child;"
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	"But if one has no power to do so, then pull it out in pieces and leave nothing of the afterbirth behind."
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	"And once you have done this, if hot boils come to the womb, apply what we have said for boiling wounds;"
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	"and if there is bleeding, put it in cooling water and apply other dressings."
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	"I saw a woman whose belly was bitten by one child, then another came out on top of it and killed the other."
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	"After some time, an abscess formed in her cheek and swelled until it opened, and then there was a great flow of pus."
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	"I was called to heal her, but I thought for a long time and could not hold the wound closed."
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	"I applied a plaster with strong attraction, and after some days one bone came out, and later another one did as well."
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	"I was very amazed because the belly has no bones."
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	"So I thought that they were the bones of a dead child."
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	"I cleaned the wound and pulled out many bones until the woman improved;"
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	"and the woman lived for a long time like that, with a little hole always leaking pus;"
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	"This chapter is recorded only so that when the master finds something strange, he may know how to treat it."
dou ramener la marris a son leu	"How to return the womb to its place"
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	"Next comes the figure of the press, with which books are printed; and at two turns around the two keys of the two lions."
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	"Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle in their restriction, and made of ivory or boxwood;"
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	"And the mouth of the wood should be two fingers wide, and the margin of the boards one finger wide, and half a palm long;"
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	"And in the middle of the two lions there should be two attachments of this same wood, which close at one end and the other, half a palm long or a little more;"
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	"And these two attachments are inserted into the mouth of the womb to open it when one turns the two horns."
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	"Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ivory or boxwood, resembling tongs;"
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	"And it should have two attachments at each end, as you see here, half a palm long and two fingers wide;"
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	"When you want to open the womb with all the instruments, have the woman lie on her back on a bed, with her feet hanging down and her legs spread apart,"
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	"then insert the two attachments together into the womb, and hold the end of the instrument underneath between her thighs;"
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	"then open your hand on the instrument just like you would with tongs, according to how much you want to open the mouth of the womb, until the child comes out as it wishes."
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	"These instruments are all mounted and have many similar forms. When the master has prepared them, the faster he works, the higher they are raised for men because of their size."
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	"Do not disdain any instrument that you have not prepared, for their necessity cannot be excused."
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	"When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must command the woman to hold her breath, then make her sneeze with condriment, and block her mouth and nose with your hands;"
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	"And if she faints because of it, so much the better."
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	"If not, take a pot and make a hole in the lid, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centory;"
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	"all these herbs or some of them should be cooked in the pot with water over the fire. Then put one end of a tube into the hole of the pot and the other end into the mouth of the womb;"
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	"and do this until the steam reaches the womb, then make her sneeze as we have said."
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	"If the afterbirth comes out quickly."
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	"And if the afterbirth still remains after this treatment and does not come out, command the midwife to wet her left hand in sesame oil or white soapwort, then put it inside."
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	"and search for the afterbirth. When she finds it, let her grasp it gently and pull it out straight little by little so that the womb does not tear;"
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	"but she must move it gently to the right and left, then pull it out. It will come and release itself."
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	"And if the mouth of the womb is very narrow, we have described the treatment of sneezing and fumigation with herbs;"
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	"And if it is not as we have said, then guard that you do not err in the treatment;"
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	"But it is necessary to tie what is at the mouth of the uterus to the woman's hip, and then apply a four-drug ointment enema;"
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	"If it [the dislocation] rises and returns, and comes forth, but nevertheless, when it rises an unpleasant odor comes to the stomach and head, and harms the patient."
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	"Therefore it is necessary to perform fumigations appropriate for this [condition]; some of the ancients have tried fumigation with mustard and dried figs."
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	"The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain the flowers [menstrual flow] and the afterbirth is this:"
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	"And it resembles a vessel made of glass, with the narrow end placed within the woman's nature [vagina], and the wide ends upon the fire;"
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	"and let the fumigation be performed on coals, replacing the wick until it is consumed, and then starting another one."
de percier lou fondement	"to pierce the anus"
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born whose anus has not been pierced, but has instead been stopped up by some fine membrane:"
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	"Therefore it is necessary for the midwife to pierce this membrane with her thumb and not with a sharp instrument, and guard that she does not touch it."
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Then apply moistened linen in wine and oil, then the treatment of ointment until it is healed."
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	"And if you doubt that [the anus] will not open up again, then place a small tube made of lead into the perforation and leave it there for several days, removing it when the child is ready to go to bed."
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	"And sometimes this obstruction comes from a sudden wound or abscess; it is necessary to cover this sudden [wound]: if it is cured, then treat it as we have said for the lead tube."
de la fistule dou fondement	"of a fistula of the anus"
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	"Fistulas which come from beneath the anus are narrow, and those which come from near the anus before or between the two buttocks,"
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	"if there is one fistula or several; and when that narrow [fistula] is ancient, then it opens up, and becomes moist with white matter or thin pus,"
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	"and sometimes these fistulas persist; and they are recognized by this: when the patient evacuates, there is discharge or wind escaping from them, and sometimes a worm comes out."
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	"And there are fistulas which penetrate as far as the bladder and as far as halfway along the penis; and they reach as far as the hip joint and as far as the thigh."
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	"And thus one recognizes a persistent fistula of the anus, and not a non-persistent one:"
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	"and this is how you do it: insert your two index fingers into the anus and insert a fine needle made of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity."
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	"And if there is tortuosity, then insert a fine lead wire or one horse hair as far as you feel the wire or hair with your finger."
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	"and if you do not feel it, and nothing comes out of the perforation – neither discharge nor wind nor worm, as we have said:"
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	"know that it does not penetrate; so hurry to cure it."
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	"And when the fistula is persistent as far as the bladder or as far as the passage of urine, then urine comes out and it cannot be healed by medications."
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	"If it penetrates as far as the hip joint, then the wire comes out at that place;"
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	"if there is no tortuosity and the pain is not continuous around it, then it is that pus continually comes out of it, and neither medication nor healing by ointment is useful."
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	"and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure but labor, and the vain boasting of foolish physicians who meddle with them."
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	"In that which is not persistent and is not ancient, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced,"
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	"And this is how it should be done: the patient lies on their stomach with their legs raised up to the hips and their hips inclined towards their belly;"
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	"then insert a wire made of brass or lead, if there is tortuosity, as far as you know where the wire comes out."
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	"If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must insert your two index fingers into it,"
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	"then feel carefully that the wire has pierced it; and if you feel between your finger the sphincter or the flesh, then know that it is persistent;"
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	"otherwise do not labor over it, for one cannot heal it."
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	"It is said nonetheless that some can be healed, but this happens rarely;"
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	"And the help that one does there is to heat a fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it is said before;"
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	"and insert it hot into the fistula until it reaches the anus and do this two or three times, so that you know that the broken flesh is burned, which resembles a feather of a bird;"
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	"and then treat it with moistened wires smeared in butter until the flesh comes out again, and then treat it with ointment to heal the surrounding flesh."
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	"If it is healed like this, that's good. But if not, then it cannot be healed otherwise;"
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	"And if the wire enters but does not reach your finger that is in the anus, and there is a thick covering of flesh or sphincter between your two fingers and the wire, and you see the fistula at the end of the covering of the heart;"
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	"then cut off the beginning of the fistula and push the wire further ahead, then heat the cautery afterwards until it reaches the tip of the wire;"
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	"and the wire will be delivered and fall out; then burn away those broken flesh that resemble a feather of a bird, so that none remains."
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	"And if the skin is thin and cuts between you and your work, then cauterize it with fire or strong medication."
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	"For the cautery of fire performs two things at once: namely, burning those neighboring flesh, and closing off blood vessels and drying up moisture;"
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	"then treat it with moistened wires smeared in butter or bruised herbs until the place is clean and the burned flesh comes out in the pus;"
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	"then heal the wound with healing ointments that surround hard flesh, which are dry medications."
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	"For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not return again."
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	"And if a fistula comes from deep within the anus and is far from the body, insert your two fingers into the anus and search for it."
