Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if fine veins appear on the surface even after a long time, do not despair about recovery
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For healing approaches. For there are men for whom it takes a long time to regenerate flesh in their wounds, and others who are the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	And if painful swelling comes back to the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healed yet.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	And if the breast takes a long time to heal and becomes dry, apply drying medicines moist in substance but dry in nature
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	Such as diaphoretic ointment, for there is a large portion of vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take diaphoretic ointment, which they make with rose oil, and rose water equal in amount
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	Then cook it down and use it; and this is also done better with honey increased
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	When diaphoretic ointment is not available
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	Then take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them together, and powder them over the honey while it's on the fire
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	And then put one bandage in it, apply it to the breast, and administer a long astrology once in a while
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	And roots of celestine lily, which is also like white flour and barley flour
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	And use simple herbs or composites: grind them up, make powder from them, put it on the honey I mentioned earlier, and apply it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	And if the cure is prolonged, and not cured by this treatment
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	Then know that the corruption has gone deep, and made an impression on the bone, or there are hard members or ligaments.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	If it is a cure for fistula, as we have said earlier.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the aposteme of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is an aposteme that arises under the nail of the little finger of the hand
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or foot, or sometimes it can arise in other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	"And when it is old, and no care is taken, there comes a hot ulcer."
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	"They will run and strike the bone so much that they will reach the root of the nail, and sometimes they will even reach all the way to it."
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	"And corrosion comes as far as the bone, so that there is foul-smelling pain, and the skin becomes swollen in two places, and the color is dark."
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	"When you treat it as we have said in the chapter on dislocation, but the treatment does not help,"
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	It is necessary that you cut off one finger's width of all the excess skin that has remained from the nail.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization provides much assistance if the bone is healthy, and the nail is sound;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses into the flesh and begins to pierce it, causing bleeding;
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	If you must place the hot iron under the nail where the flesh points
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and strike it upwards, cutting that delicate flesh gently
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and place on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove all of it;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply dressings until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and cauterize it, for as long as corrupted bone remains there, it will not heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see both bones rotting, cut one off as it is stated above
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply dressings until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is infected and festers, causing great pain, you must first heal it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	Then cut the nail of the spur at an angle across from above
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and ensure that the cut does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel great pain
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it does, put something on to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain in the wrist
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	Some men may have a joint next to theirs that is completely fatty
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes it has bones, and other times it has a nail
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	but none of these grow from the root of the joint, where they are born in some fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that grow on any knuckle of the finger do not move
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that grow at the joint of the finger may move;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The waist of one who is fleshly is light, in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	taille lui à la racine d'un large spatule.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; so be careful with him.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	For those who are born in the root or joint of the shoulder blade, it is necessary that you first cut around the flesh up to the bone
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, then cure it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The dislocations that occur at both hips come either by birth or from a wound, or from burns, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	You must cut this dislocation so that the thighbone returns to its natural shape;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between both a wet cloth or bandage soaked in rose oil so that they do not heal together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	"Place two thin pieces of lead between them until the joint is tightly wedged as it ought to be."
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	"If one's elbow comes apart with the palm of his hand, then cut that bone just like so."
Des vils	Of warts
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Warts are large tumors filled with melancholic excesses that appear on various parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they happen more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry things than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer to him a purge for the stomach and then the holy oil from the church.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with iron is done in two ways: one is by cutting them off, and the other is to draw out the black blood from them.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	"And another manner is thus: you open the vein and draw out all the blood."
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	"The operation proceeds in this way: first, raise the leg with very hot water until the thick skin becomes soft,"
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	"then press the leg of the sick person downwards from above the hip to below the knee;"
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the vein at one place, or two, or three, of a wide size
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then squeeze and pull forcefully to release black blood from the hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood exits as the patient's condition can tolerate.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bandage it, and tell him/her to compress with fresh meat around the black wound.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and begin again the evacuation and cleaning when the veins are full, harming the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The lifting of the leg is done in this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if it has much hair
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put him/her in a bath and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you don’t have a bath, heat it by fire and then cut near the vein at the long bone of the knee or in the part below the ankle
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then cover with an ointment of hog's grease and scrape away the vein from each side until it becomes visible when touched
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and when seen, it appears red and black, and when it enters into the skin, it seems like a white rope
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then place the knife underneath until the vein is lifted from the skin, and then cut it with hog's grease lightly
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut again in another place three fingers away; then scrape away the skin above the vein until it becomes visible
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it with the knife, as you have done before, and cut it with another hog's grease, as you did first
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then make another incision, or several if necessary, then lift the vein and cut it at the two ends of the foot
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then tie it and lift it up to the second incision; then extract it from incision to incision until it comes out entirely, then cut it
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull it out and lift it, then insert a strong doubled thread needle
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie it and pull it, and place a knife underneath, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And be sure that it does not break, for if it breaks, you cannot pull or lift it and harm will come to the patient
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have entirely pulled it out, put on the wound wool moistened with wine and rose oil; and dress it until it is clean.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and convoluted together, and is not straight as we have said
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then you must cut it crookedly but do not break it; and pull it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the knife used to cut the vein is curved, so that it does not cut the vein itself
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is thickly curved, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein; but let it be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
De la voinne civile	"Of the civil vein"
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in legs, in hot regions where no herbs or trees grow, and on land with no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And sometimes it appears elsewhere than in the legs, which happens due to rot that forms under the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	"As serpents and worms enter the body, twisting between skin and flesh."
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	"And if the sign of the onset of this vein is that there comes a very great inflammation in the leg,"
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	"then the location changes, and the vein begins to burst forth like the root of a plant."
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	"When the flesh opens up, you must wrap around it a piece of linen two and a half to three fingers wide."
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	"and let the linen hang down on the leg; and every time it comes out again at the front, wrap it around the linen."
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	"and if it is too long, cut off a piece of it, and wrap the remaining part around it, but do not cut off its root until it has all come out."
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	"for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh and cause an abscess and decay in that place, and bad sickness;"
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	"because of this, it is necessary to treat it little by little until it reaches its head, and nothing remains in the body."
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	"And sometimes this vein, once treated for five or ten palms of length,"
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	"and once there came to me a man whose vein was twenty palms in length; and when you cut it, it throws out one ray or opening, and pierces through to the bottom,"
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	"so that it all comes out; and let the matter inside be emptied, and apply medicinal herbs to prevent decay for a few days, then heal it as you would a boil."
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	"And sometimes this vein has many rays, especially when it opens up at the ankle joint or on the foot,"
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	"And much loss occurs, and from which rain flows; therefore treat it as we have said before."
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	"Worms that are born between skin and flesh"
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	"This illness is called in our land 'cattle disease', because it happens often to cattle,"
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	"and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body ascending and descending,"
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	"And one can feel it well when moving from limb to limb until it reaches the skin where it went out; thus:"
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	"and is caused by corruption of certain humours, such as come worms and serpents and shadows and roundworms in the belly;"
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	"And one doubts its harmfulness, for when it goes through the body, it ascends to the head and comes to the eye,"
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	"and sometimes enters it and destroys the eye; and this happens often."
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	"When you see him cured and treated, then one can be sure only when he has left:"
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	"So it is necessary that you tie the loop above and below with a strong, tightly drawn knot,"
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	"then cut upwards and draw it out; and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you do not find it,"
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	"then cauterize it with fire until it dies;"
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	"And the greatest harm that it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said;"
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	"And if you see it coming towards the head near the eye, press down on it firmly with a finger, then cut upwards and draw it out;"
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	"It is necessary to use medicinal remedies for cleansing the body of corrupted humours,"
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	"and beware of foods that cause corruption."
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	About the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	"This illness is called in our land ' vakir ', and is a pain that comes in certain limbs,"
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	"And then it moves from limb to limb; and I have seen this, as I tell you."
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	"I was called to see a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the bend of the elbow;"
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	"and soon after, I saw it move like a worm up to the shoulder,"
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	"swifter than anything else, just like quicksilver when it runs from one place to another;"
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	"The pain departed from that spot and stuck in the shoulder,"
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	"and then a little later it corrupted throughout her body until it came to the other arm;"
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	"then she told me that it was constantly turning around her body, as I saw it."
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	"I wondered greatly how it could move thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness behave in this manner."
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	"Nevertheless, I had often heard of pains moving from one place to another,"
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	"but I had never seen it thus, as I saw it in this woman;"
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	"I thought that this was because the woman had a thin body and uncovered joints,"
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	"and because of that, the windiness seemed constrained;"
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	"And those who are delicate and have moist bodies and covered joints do not appear to suffer from this."
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	"When you see that this illness has been cured, if the sick person still feels pain as we have described,"
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	"then tie above and below quickly and then cut upwards until that constrained wind comes out;"
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	"And cauterize the spot, and if you do not see it with your eyes,"
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	"then treat it with remedies that expel windiness, such as fetid pills and pills of saffron, etc."
Des saiettes	Of Hemorrhoids
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	"Hemorrhoids are various in appearance and according to the parts of the body where they are found."
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	"Their varieties include those that have large points, small ones, hairy ones, and smooth ones;"
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	"and those that have two points, those with tongues, and those with lumps."
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	"And they discharge from certain limbs in two ways: either from the principal limb with hair,"
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	"such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder and similar parts;"
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	"When they discharge from any of these parts and the sign of death that I will tell you about appears:"
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	"You must beware of extracting this hemorrhoid because death can follow in many cases;"
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	"but if this sign does not appear and the hemorrhoid is not deep, then treat it and heal the wound."
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	"The sign of a cerebral hemorrhoid occurs when it discharges there and pierces the bone, causing the brain substance that lies above the brain to spill out;"
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	"and when there is dimness of sight and loss of hearing and giddiness and redness in the eyes and inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and mixture of understanding, vomiting of bile;"
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	"and sometimes there is blood from the nostrils or ears, and sometimes speech and voice are lost;"
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	"And sometimes white moist pus like chicken meat comes out of the wound, and also burns like a branding iron;"
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	"If this sign appears to you, then beware of treating it, and extract the hemorrhoid if it is not inflamed."
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	"The signs of a cardiac hemorrhoid are that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty;"
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	"And sometimes the hemorrhoid moves like a chicken, and black blood flows out, followed by coldness and cold sweat, and syncope;"
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	"Then know for certain that death is approaching."
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	"The signs of a hemorrhoid that affects the lungs include foaming without pain coming out of the wound, swelling of the throat, change in color of the patient, loud sighing, and seeking cold air."
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	"If a hemorrhoid appears on the chest covering near the ribs, there is much wheezing and pain and sighing, and all the shoulders move."
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	"And if a hemorrhoid appears in the stomach, digested food may sometimes come out of the wound."
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	"And if a hemorrhoid appears in the abdomen and dark feces come out of the intestines, then there is no hope of recovery or extraction of the hemorrhoid."
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	"And if a hemorrhoid appears in the bladder and urine flows out with feces and the patient feels strong pain, know that the wound is fatal."
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	"Other parts such as the face, neck, throat, shoulders, arms, backbones, thighs, buttocks, legs and similar parts are safe from hemorrhoids in many cases."
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	"When a hemorrhoid appears on a nerve or artery that is not venomous, as happened to me once so that you may do the same if necessary."
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	"It happened to one man that a hemorrhoid fell on his eyelid at the root of his nose:"
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	"I tried it and extracted it from another spot below the ear fat, and he was healed without any damage."
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	"And I extracted a hemorrhoid that fell into the ear fat under the skin of the cheek in one stroke:"
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	"and the hemorrhoid was covered and I could only grasp its tip facing the wood;"
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	"and the hemorrhoid was as big as an archery bowstring, one finger wide without ears; the patient was healed and suffered no bad consequences."
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	"And extracted a hemorrhoid from the throat of a Christian, and the hemorrhoid was Arabic with ears:"
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	"I shaved his beard, and I worked so subtly that he didn't notice it, and the Christian was healed."
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	"And gave one man a cup to drink from, which had fallen onto his belly, thinking that he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	"and after thirty days had passed, he did not move at all;"
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut upon the arrowhead, and sharpened it, and drew it forth, and there was no ill effect.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a man with an arrow stuck in his back that has healed over.
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remained inside him and did not change its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	"No harm is found in any of its natural works."
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	"And behold another man, upon whom a tile fell on his face, and the wound was healed;"
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others similarly.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	"And he carried a tile to one of the king's princes, which had fallen into his nose,"
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was slightly tilted towards the right side; and the tile was completely covered
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat him after three days had passed, and I found the wound very narrow
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I opened it with a fine needle, but did not feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and discomfort beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought that it was from the tip of the tile
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I applied there a plaster made of attratif and digestive medicine, so that the wound would not become inflamed;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and then appeared the tip of the tile.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied this plaster for several days, and the wound healed again, and the patient remained thus for a long time
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the tile one day inside his nose, and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied a medicine of aqua corrosiva to the wound for many days until it was opened again
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I probed it and felt the head of the tile which was stuck there;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I used this same medicine to gradually dilate the opening of the wound until the head of the tile became clearly visible
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it took more than four months
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then the wound opened so much that I put forceps in and pulled on either side, but could not remove it;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not cease to experiment and devise various ways of instruments until I finally grasped the tile with well-made forceps one day
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	as described in the end of this chapter, so that I pulled it out and closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	So I closed it up again and the wound was healed, and the patient recovered completely
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you about the extraction of some tiles
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you can apply your treatment based on what I did not say, for books cannot cover everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters compare even small things and what is present and lacking
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find nine works and nine instruments for the handling of strange occurrences in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that tiles come out of their members where they are stuck only in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the place where they entered or through another part
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And those that come out of the same place where they entered are called entering tiles, and sometimes they come out by themselves;
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out by itself, then let it remain until the flesh around it is fully corrupted and the exit is cleared;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in bone and cannot come out, then leave it for some days, and soften the flesh around it daily with medicine
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will come out; if not, then carefully pierce all around it with a fine needle until the area is widened, and then pull it out
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the tile is stuck in the bone of the head and goes as far as one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	"And among the accidents I mentioned, some are apparent to the patient. Therefore, do not pull it out immediately, but wait until it becomes even after several days."
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	"For if the blade comes up to here, that is called the hilt."
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	"And if the blade is stuck only in the bone and does not come up to the hilt,"
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	"and the patient remains for several days without any bad accidents, then you can attempt to pull it out."
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if it is very deeply stuck and cannot come out otherwise, then you should administer compresses around it, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healthy."
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	"And if the blade has penetrated into the flesh of the body so that one cannot see it, search for it carefully with your hand."
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	"and if you feel it, then pull it out with some suitable instrument;"
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	"And if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the blade,"
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	"then cut around it until the wound is large;"
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	"and pull out the blade if you can, and if there are ears on the blade where it is stuck,"
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	"then cut away the flesh that is stuck in it by two parts as much as you can."
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	"And then break or bend back the ears of the blade so that you can pull it out;"
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	"and be careful not to break the blade as you pull it out."
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	"And if you cannot pull it out all at once, leave it until the wound around it is clean, then pull it out, for extraction will be easier."
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	"And if bleeding makes you hesitate, then administer what we have said about treatment in its chapter;"
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	"and beware of cutting the nerve and the vein, and try to pull out the blade as gently as possible without danger."
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	"Sooner or later, firmly or gently, put the patient back into the position they were in when the blade fell in."
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	"for that is the greatest help there can be. And if you cannot do this, then place them according to what the signs show you."
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	"A blade that comes out on its own from another side, or where some part of it can be seen, or where the skin is swollen around it and can be seen or felt apart:"
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	"then cut above it so that forceps can grasp it, then pull it out: if it comes out now."
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	"And if it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand around it until it enters the bone, then widen the bone and pull it out."
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	"And if it cannot come out, leave it alone for now, and then try again to extract it until it comes out;"
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	"and if the hilt of the blade remains in place, remove the whole handle;"
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	"And if the handle falls off and you need to administer a blow, then use one of these instruments:"
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	"So that the point of the blade enters the notch of the instrument; then strike it out;"
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	"And if the blade is stuck in bone, use one of these instruments with an entering point to facilitate extraction."
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	"If the blade has touched a vein, you must cut away all the flesh around where the vein is, if possible;"
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	"then treat the wound as it should be treated."
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	"And if the blade falls on the thigh or belly or bladder or side and is close by, and you can cut towards it, then cut towards it;"
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	"and beware of cutting the vein and nerve, then pull out the blade, then sew up the wound if necessary."
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	"And treat it until it is healed."
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	"The shape of forceps used to treat blades is like the beak of a bird, as shown here:"
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	"And there are many kinds of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the blade."
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	"The shape of the striking instrument is also like the feather of a bird,"
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	"to strike at the point of the blade, as shown here:"
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	"The shape of forceps for striking and holding is as follows:"
des voinnes dou cors communes	"for the common veins of the body:"
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	"There are 31 veins that can be used to heal oneself, with 16 at the head."
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	"That is to say, there are two bat's-wing veins behind the ears, called the 'dous herbech';"
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	"and the two arteries that are visible in the two temples;"
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	"And the two veins in the inner corners of the two eyes, called 'aspirants';"
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	"and the vein that is within the forehead; and the vein at the nose's tip;"
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	"And the two jugular veins in the neck;"
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	"and the two veins that are above the mouth's lips, called 'augeherich';"
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	"And two veins under the tongue."
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	"The five veins commonly used for healing in each arm are:"
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	"One is the cephalic vein, on the left side of the chest, called by laypeople 'the vein of the head';"
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	"And the middle one is called 'fast', composed of the cephalic and basilic veins;"
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	"and laypeople call it 'the vein of the heart'; and the basilic vein is on the right side of the chest;"
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	"And they call it 'the vein of the belly', and it is above the palmaris longus;"
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	"It is this one that we use for healing, which appears clearly at the elbow."
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	"And the salvation vein is the one between the little finger and ring finger, with two branches;"
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	"In the leg and foot there are three veins: one beneath the bend of the left knee,"
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	"And the second saphenous vein at the ankle on the right side; and the 'nese' vein in the ankle of the other side;"
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	"and in the other leg there are three veins below these."
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	"Healing with the veins behind the ears helps those who are elderly and prone to headaches;"
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	"And the qualities of healing, as I told you, include raising the sick person's head,"
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	"and rubbing the place where the veins are with rough cloth; then have the sick person tighten their collar with a vise;"
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	"So that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head:"
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	"Then take hold of them with your thumb and forefinger, and where you feel the pulse beneath your fingers, squeeze gently;"
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	"then take the lancet and insert it below the vein until it reaches bone, then raise your hand upstream along the entire vein;"
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	"And cut both skin and vein well with two fingers' width, and let blood flow until you see that it does;"
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	"then bind it and tie it until it is healed."
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	"And I have already described the incision and cautery in the first book."
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	"Healing with the two arteries in the temples helps those who are elderly and prone to headaches;"
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	"and those who suffer from coldness, and customary eye inflammation, and watery eyes caused by ailing of the body;"
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	"And the qualities of healing are as I told you:"
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	"It is that the sick person tightens their collar until the two veins appear clearly;"
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	"And feels their pulse beneath your fingers, then squeeze gently;"
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	"then raise the heart above the vein with your index finger, and insert the lancet below it;"
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	"And raise the vein upwards, and cut it, just as you did on two other veins, and let blood flow according to your need."
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then bandage the patient, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	Then tie it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; we have already spoken about their dressing and extraction at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the frontal vein is just as valuable as that of the temporal vein for treating old facial diseases, migraines, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	Its quality is such that the patient twists their neck until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called "the chisel", of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	Place the point on the vein and strike it with your hand or something else, allowing blood to flow according to the desired amount.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then untie the patient's neck and tie the vein tightly until it is healed, sometimes using a wide bandage.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, be careful not to tie the bandages too tightly; also heal it diagonally because the bone is nearby, and by chance the bandage might break if it's too thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in the temples helps with eye diseases, baldness, redness, inflammation around the eye, and facial diseases.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	Its quality is such that the patient twists their neck without any tie, just like before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then heal it diagonally with a bandage that is somewhat long and somewhat wide because there is no flesh in that area.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bandage is too thin, it might break; then allow blood to flow until you have enough, and then tie a cotton pad on top and tie it securely.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The healing of the vein in the nose is beneficial for fevers, frenzy, and facial diseases,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	As migraines and redness come to the face, especially when it is chronic;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the characteristic of the sickness is that the patient strains their neck, then stretches their nose towards your left hand
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and takes a long thin reed and places it between the two nostrils
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the airway does not open well there, and the breath will now begin to flow
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not blow too deeply, allowing blood to flow according to your need, then leave it for a night as it is quickly restored
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the shape of the reed:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The inflammation of the two glands aids in the stretching of tendons and the beginning of hernias, and helps with many diseases, including dropsy, corrosion, herpes, and sciatica
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the characteristic of this sickness is that the patient strains their neck to both sides as we have mentioned
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And let the master stand on top of the patient's head and the patient sit on a chair
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then open the airway widely for about an inch, then draw blood temperately or as much is needed
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then repeat on the other vein, then untie the ligature and gently press on both veins
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	that the patient does not strangle themselves, and leave it until morning when the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the treatment for lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The treatment for veins above the lips helps with:
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	"And the quality of the cautery is to make the patient sit before you, and hold their neck steady as I have said;"
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	"Then turn your attention to the lips, and look at two vessels, one on the right lip and one on the left."
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	"And recognize them by their darkness, and also by the small dark veins around them:"
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	"So cut both of them, but if you do not recognize them or are in doubt,"
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	"If you cannot, then cut the largest of each side, and also do the same for the two veins that are above and below them, as this is the same method."
De la sainie desoz la lengue	"On cauterizing under the tongue"
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	"The cautery of the veins that are under the tongue helps afterwards the cautery of the cephalic vein, and it is for the tightness of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth;"
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	"And the quality of the cautery is that the patient should sit facing you in sunlight, raise their tongue and look underneath on either side for a black vein:"
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	"So cauterize both of them, but do not go too deep, as the arteries are underneath."
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	"The veins on the neck which are commonly cauterized are done in two ways:"
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	"Either by gripping with one wide flame of mirt, or by cutting thinly and sharply like a chisel, which is called 'anesil';"
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	"And they are wide and thin according to the size and narrowness of the veins."
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	"The shape of the flame of mirt is very well-known, and it is wide as you can see:"
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	"And it is necessary for opening the veins that are flat on the head, containing thick and turbid blood;"
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	"and this is the shape of the olive flame:"
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	"And it is more pointed and sharp, and is for cauterizing small veins where there is thin citrine blood."
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	"The cautery of the cephalic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, neck, and chest, and in the belly;"
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	"And the cauterizer must cauterize skillfully and be careful of the artery that is underneath."
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	"If he cuts the artery, and blood flows out, then he should stop it by cauterizing, as I have said;"
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	"And the flame should not be pointed but cutting like a chisel."
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	"If the cephalic vein does not open clearly, then you must draw it out and change to another one;"
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	"or you want any branch of it, or you cauterize in its place the vein on the arm which opens clearly;"
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	"And cut it with the flame chisel-shaped, as we have said."
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	"If you wish to know where to cauterize, then it is necessary beforehand to draw out the arm, and touch the place until you feel the pulse;"
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	"then mark the place with ink, then tie the arm, and cut the vein with the flame chisel-shaped."
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	"And be careful not to strike the artery when you see the place swelling, for it is the artery; avoid it therefore."
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	"And if you see something coming out above like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood;"
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	"So hurry up then, and put your finger on it for a while, then remove your finger when the bleeding stops, which happens many times;"
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	"then tie the arm and leave it like that, and do not let the sick person move it; he should be careful and not move it until he is healed."
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	"And if the blood does not stop and you faint, and a physician is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, because its head withdraws. Then stop the bleeding."
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	"And take an incision of fisticus (fig tree), cut it in half, and take one half and tie it on tightly until the next day;"
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	"If the bleeding stops, that's good. If not, then cure it with powders that stop bleeding, as we have said."
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	"And the cauterization should not be feared in many positions for the small place of the wound and the strength of the ligature of the arm."
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	"The cautery of the vein in the middle helps to draw blood from the head above and from the body below,"
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	"because it is composed of the cephalic and basilica veins, as we have said;"
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	"And the cauterizer must be careful about the nerve underneath, and if he does not go too deep, he will find the nerve;"
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	"and it swells and the sick person is harmed, and perhaps he cannot heal."
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	"And this nerve opens very often, and if it does not open in some people because of its thinness, then you should cauterize it with the chisel-shaped instrument. And avoid the nerve as much as possible."
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	"And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it lengthwise."
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	"The cautery of the cephalic vein helps to draw blood from the head and helps with eyestrain;"
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	"And it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed flame shaped like an olive or myrtle, because this vein is the safest of all veins since there are neither nerve nor artery underneath."
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	"Nevertheless, it is necessary to look for the easiest place, and do not worry if you fail the first time. Then start again;"
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	"And perhaps the place swells in some people when they fail the first time, but it does not matter."
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	"The quality of cautery depends on your skill."
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	"The first thing you should know about cauterization is that cautery is not undertaken for any other reason than to maintain health;"
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	"and to avoid future illnesses."
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	"And cautery should be performed on one of the three veins that are located on the arm: namely, the cephalic, basilic, and median cephalic veins;"
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	"And cautery should be performed at the beginning of Lent, in autumn and winter after meals when signs of repletion appear;"
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	"And cauterization should be done on the first or third day, two or three hours after noon."
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	"The cautery performed for illnesses has no fixed time, but it should be done whenever necessary, day or night, at any hour."
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	"And children should not be cauterized until they are twelve years old, nor women except from the fourth month to seven months of pregnancy."
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	"Nor should old people over sixty years old be cauterized."
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	"And when someone wants to be cauterized in any way, it is necessary that they cleanse their intestines with a light clyster;"
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	"because if there is much retained feces, then the veins cannot draw the impurities from the intestines to nourish the principal members;"
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	"nor should one cauterize those who are too fond of meat or drunkards until they are sober again. Nor should one cauterize those with dropsy."
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	"And one should be cautious about cauterizing after colic attacks, vomiting, diarrhea, laborious childbirth, excessive menstrual flow in women, hard work, watching and fasting, and those who are entirely lacking virtue or have a disease of the limbs or body."
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	"Then thin out the humors if they are thick by eating and drinking properly, and taking medicine if you have the power to do so;"
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then enter between the bath, if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and cleanse the vein of the breast around the third rib, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And guard yourself that day from work, and pain, and lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And be glad and joyful, and may the healthier one be higher than the one who is being supported, and let the companion wipe his arm twice or three times
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then loosen the bandage in the middle because if it is too tight or small, the wound cannot heal.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then wipe the area with his hands until the veins swell and can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then let the healthier one moisten the flame of a little bit of old oil on his right hand thumb, then place his left hand index finger on the vein under the wound where he wants to support
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	So that the vein does not break or split when struck.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that flee like strings from the wound, and there are such as are full of wind
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts on the flame, it draws back with the flame, and cannot open the vein, such are some.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if it opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, therefore one must be skillful in these matters for the supporting.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens at first, that's good. If not, then begin again a little below or above hastily, if the wound is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the wound is swollen and the patient is frightened, let it rest for one or two days without binding the arm
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	lest chance phlegm may come; do not enter into a bath, then begin again the supporting if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the opening is small or the wound closes subtly and you doubt that it is not flowing enough blood as you wish, then put all the flame directly into that opening itself.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And open it a little hastily before the wound becomes swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the wound swollen, do not begin supporting again and put on a little bit of oil and honey mixture, for it lightens the body's blood and is healing in this wound the honey that comes from the hive.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the mixture of oil every time you support the veins to stanch the flow of blood
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same thing draws together and closes up the wound when put upon it, so that the blood may flow more subtly and spread out when it is too abundant.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if a large phlegm comes, which happens often, especially when the vein is not supported but at that time when the opening of the vein is small
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	then hurry and put on a sponge moistened in water and hot salt, and hold it there for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And you must do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if some blackness or greenness remains on the wound for a few days afterward, it will not harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see any blackness or greenness remaining on the wound, put on some ointment of aloe or myrrh mixed with juice of calamint, marjoram, or similar herbs.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there appears phlegm and swelling during the supporting of the basilica (vein): therefore put your hand on it, and if you find the wound soft under the pressure of your hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be sure not to put on anything of those things that we have said, for perhaps the wound may close up the artery; but make one plaster dry to harden the wound, then cure it with another plaster until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each person according to the quantity of his strength and the color of his blood
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if it flows abundantly, let it flow until it becomes more subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for those who are full and strong, and have need of blood-letting, that they should make a larger wound and use broader lancet
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for those who are weak, do the opposite: let them be supported less and more often, and they should be supported by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this manner of supporting saves from losing blood and tearing the nerves, and is more useful than supporting by cutting long or broad.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for those whose body is weak from supporting, it is necessary to give them bread moistened in pomegranate juice to drink; if they are feverish, let three or four blood-lettings be done upon them.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if they are of cold temperament, let them eat before the blood-letting bread moistened in sweet syrup or spiced honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cumin, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if they faint during the blood-letting after losing much blood, it is necessary that they should smell broth of meat and subtly scented syrup
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things that we have said in the chapter on syncope for evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to let out some blood from his arm and be supported again later, when he is weakened by much blood-letting, it is necessary that he should be supported a little at a time according to the quantity of his remaining strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to let out some blood from his arm after the first blood-letting and has a strong body, should be supported again seven hours after the first blood-letting or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to be supported on another part of his body, should be supported on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood in the body that has already been heated up and causes fever; therefore it is necessary to draw a large quantity of blood, and to make the wound wide enough for it to flow freely.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	Then, after all preparations for blood-letting have been made and your hand is placed on the vein when it is being let out, make sure that the mouth does not come into contact with the wound.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	And this often happens through the carelessness of the blood-letter
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	But it is necessary to press strongly upon the wound when you see that the arm has to be unbound and blood let out a second time, and if the wound has closed.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	Otherwise, if the arm is bent, it should be extended quickly, for otherwise it would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	But let the blood flow until it flows again the second time; or you can prick with the point of the lancet until the blood that has frozen at the mouth of the vein flows out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Then put on a little salt moistened in water and press lightly upon it.
