Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has swollen up, let it alone and do not compress it until the inflammation is eased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if there is necessity to draw blood a second time, then let it out in the same vein or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are supported in place of those in the head because they are composed (i.e., contain many branches).
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of blood-letting is this: the sick person immerses his hand in warm water until the veins become red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	"Then gently tie it so that the vein appears well, then press the sinew from across, not from wide nor long;"
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	"And let the hole be wide, and let it be carefully cut near the joint of the hand; if any bone protrudes, put the hand in warm water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough;"
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	"And if it is summer, do not put the hand in warm water, because one puts it more often in winter than in summer;"
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	"The cutting of this vein is safer than that of any other veins, since there is neither artery nor nerve there."
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	"The cutting of the vein on the back of the right hand is beneficial for all diseases of the liver, and this is how:"
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	"Press the hand and put it in warm water until the vein swells and can be seen;"
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	"And if you cut across it, and cut it entirely along its length, nothing will be harmed;"
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	"And do not go too deep, for the nerves are all underneath, covered with flesh,"
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	"And then put the hand back in warm water if the blood is congealed in the wound and cannot flow out."
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	"And when you have let out as much blood as is needed, then put oil and a bandage on the vein to heal quickly, and do the same for each vein."
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	"The cutting of the vein in the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the mouse (epilepsy), and do everything just as I have told you concerning the right hand."
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	"The cutting of the saphenous vein is beneficial for all diseases that are underneath the body;"
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	"such as diseases of the bladder, retention of urine, disease of the kidneys, and old diseases of the thighs and legs, and similar diseases."
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	"The qualities of this vein cutting are that the sick person puts his foot in warm water, and rubs the vein until it protrudes;"
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	"And places it above the ankle bone; and this vein is at the ankle, and many veins go through there into the foot;"
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	"therefore cut where the largest vein is, or at the ankle, whichever suits you best."
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	"And if you cut it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are underneath, and cut across just like cutting with scissors; and let the wound heal cleanly."
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	"And if blood cannot flow out, then put the foot back in water and let the vein drain well."
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	"If the first cutting fails, then begin again a little higher up on the second occasion, for the spot is sensitive;"
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	"do not fear damaging nerves, as we have said, and do the same for the saphenous vein of the other foot."
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	"The location of the sciatic vein is at the outer ankle bone, and its cutting is beneficial for hip pain when it is caused by hot blood."
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	"And the qualities of this vein cutting are that the sick person enters a bath, and stretches out above the ankle with four fingers twisted;"
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	"for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then cut it in all ways that you can, including across it;"
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	"and it is better that you cut it with scissors, for the spot is sensitive and it is very prone to many people."
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	"And if you cannot find it, then cut any vein that opens up on the back of the foot near the little toe, and beware of nerves;"
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	"and let out as much blood as you see fit, then untie the bandage, put cotton on it and bind it up again; now it is cut."
Des sainies de ventouse	About cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	"Cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking."
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	"And this cupping that is done without striking is of two kinds: either it is done with fire, or without fire;"
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	"and cupping that is done by striking and drawing blood is performed in fourteen places on the body:"
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	"of which one is entirely on the top of the head, and another is between the neck;"
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	"and two others are on either side of the neck, and the cupping under the chin;"
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	"and the cupping on the two shoulders, and on the buttocks;"
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	"and the cupping between the two arms, and on the two legs;"
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	"and the cupping on the two ankles; and cupping does not draw much blood, except for some small veins that are scattered in the flesh;"
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	"And therefore it does not weaken at all, as cutting veins does."
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	"and it should not be administered in any disease caused bypletion, whether with fire or without fire, until the whole body is emptied."
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	"And if it becomes necessary to cup due to disease or customs, then we will administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and both during and between each time;"
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	"for there are some people who need to cup but have heavy heads;"
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	"and others findpletion and redness in their face, head, neck, and darkness in the eyes;"
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	"And others feel a drop of blood in their mouth, have an inflamed tongue, and cough up blood;"
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	"And there are some who dream, see red blood and wounds, dead bodies and similar things."
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	"And when we see these signs, especially if it is during the month, we order them to cup after three hours of the day."
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	"The cutting of the muscle helps against headache ... that comes upon them, and it is not necessary for this to be done after evacuating the whole body;"
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	"And this cupping is in place of cutting the cephalic vein,"
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	"and those who have a cold constitution or who are phlegmatic should not use it, for this greatly harms them;"
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	"And therefore old people and those with cold diseases of the head should not use it."
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	"And those who often cut themselves become forgetful, so it is necessary to place the cupping a little lower down for fear of forgetting."
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	"Cupping on the neck is in place of cutting the head and basilica veins, and therefore it helps with chest tightness;"
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	"and it relieves heart pain, and promotes coughing and excretion;"
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	"And it should not be placed too high up, for if it holds too firmly it can cause forgetfulness or harm the stomach or heart."
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	"Cupping on either side of the neck is beneficial for headaches, eye pain and migraine, and for throat tightness and toothache;"
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	"and it is in place of cutting the basilica vein. Order the cutter to press his hand when applying it so that he does not cut the artery or veins."
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	"Cupping under the chin is beneficial for mouth diseases, gum decay, and similar conditions in the mouth, and it is in place of cutting both lips."
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	"Cupping on the shoulders helps with diseases caused by heat andpletion."
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	"Cupping on the arms is as effective as cutting three veins of the arm;"
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	"for it draws blood from these large veins;"
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	"And order the cutter not to go too deep, for the place is lacking in flesh and contains nerves and arteries."
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The leech that is placed on the buttock is beneficial for hemorrhoids of the foundation, and for diseases below. It is necessary that the leech be large, and made of brass, so it can draw well; however, if it were delicate, it might break; and it makes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	**Line-by-line translation:**
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the cupping glass is as follows: first apply it empty, and suck temperately, and place it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see that the area is red and swollen, and appears the redness of blood; then stop, and remove the cups, and take care in the position of the body, for there are some who have thin flesh and clear pores: thus one should strike once only, and make wide wounds, but not too deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, then one must strike twice: the first time to refine the passage of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, then one must strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out blood drop by drop, it suffices to strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we wish for much blood, then we recommence often; and if the blood is thick, strike deeper, and the endpoint is when the heart is pierced suddenly
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it behooves those who have thick skin and hard flesh, and who have narrow pores, to grease the places of the cups with oil that is aperient and dissolvent:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in summer, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is winter, use mustard oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, use almond oil, or balsam oil, or aniseed oil, or something similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if those whose skin is being treated have tender flesh and wide pores, it is not necessary to use any oil
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but after the cupping treatment they should wash with rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or pumpkin water, or copper water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture should rise using basil water, myrtle water, sumac water, and things of that sort.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities should rise with old wine, or succus water, or decoction of aniseed or chamomile, or other similar things
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and they should not be cupped before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath one or two hours; and they should not sleep after cupping.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it is necessary that he wash himself when he is about to be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And let those who are being treated who have a choleric humor guard against having too much blood that is hot and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	and they should take cold things such as pomegranates and endive and lettuce with basil, and similar things
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eat peas, castrated fish, moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion should take honey syrup and medium-sweet wine that is between old and new, and eat peaches, peas, small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day when he is to be cupped, he should drink more than he eats.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and sometimes it is necessary to give certain men treacle or musk before cupping or afterwards, in order to fortify the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And let the drink be subtle, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The cups that are placed without piercing are those that are placed on the liver, the womb, podagra, and on the belly, throat, loins, and buttocks; for these members do not withstand being pricked.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and one does not do this except to attract blood from member to member
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as when we place them on the breasts when the infant is being nursed; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cups on the belly and throat to reduce the member
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it relieves pain when there is congestion or stone; by its attractive virtue it sometimes draws out congestion or moves the stone from its place
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and so it does when it is placed on the liver and womb when there is retained wind
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these cups are administered empty to merely suck; sometimes they are administered together with fire, and at other times filled with tepid water
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in illnesses of the lungs, and this is done by filling the cup with hot water alone or water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cup administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	"And it should have two fingers of width and half a palm's depth, and around the middle on its side there should be one small hole, like that for inserting a needle."
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	"And it should be made of brass, smooth in front so that it does not wound the patient when placing it on the limb;"
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	"and in the middle there should be a crossbar of brass or iron to hold a wick candle."
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	"And they should come in various sizes according to the illness and the size of those who use them;"
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	"because the cupping glasses for children are different from those for adults, and those for thin people differ from those for fat ones."
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	"And one should place this cupping glass on the limb as follows:"
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	"First light the wick candle or a linen strip and place it inside the cupping glass through the crossbar that is in the cupping glass,"
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	"So that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient;"
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	"And then place it on the limb, with the two fingers directly above the hole we mentioned earlier, so that when desired, the air can be drawn out and the cupping glass removed;"
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	"And then one takes the linen strip as before, and repeats this process often if necessary."
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	"Therefore, the cupping glass used in treating pleurisy or any acute illness has no crossbar or hole, and is not made airtight except when it is full of water. It is placed on the limb alone."
et c’est li forme:	"And this is its shape:"
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	"Sanguineous cupping glasses are only made airtight for use on limbs where regular cupping glasses cannot be used due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas;"
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	"and in places lacking flesh, such as the spine or nails, and other similar areas;"
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	"And their quality is that when you find sanguineous cupping glasses that are in smooth, clear water without any scum or foam, then take them;"
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	"and place them in warm water until they are filled and have nothing inside."
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	"And then disinfect the vein and cupping glass, rub the limb until it is red, and place the sanguineous cups on it;"
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	"And when they are full and fall, if it is a place where one can use a regular cupping glass, then use one, for this is very beneficial."
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	"If not, lift the limb gently and then with water, and then squeeze it;"
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	"And if the limb becomes too dry after the sanguineous cups are removed, then dampen a linen cloth in cold water and place it on the area to cool the skin."
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	"And if there is an abundance of blood, then apply powdered vitriol or ointment or similar substances to cool and dry the skin."
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	"Or you can place half a handful of peeled fava beans on the limb, leaving them there until they become warm to the touch, which will stop the bleeding."
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	"And if more are needed, then take additional sanguineous cups."
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	"If the sanguineous cups will not adhere, then rub fresh blood onto the limb and insert a needle until blood flows out;"
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	"and place them on the area, as soon as they feel the blood they will become adherent."
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	"And when you see that they are falling, then sprinkle a little powder made from ground aloe and salt or ash on them, which will cause them to adhere again."
Ci comence li livre des brisures	"Here begins the book of fractures"
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	"This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and is a remedy for fracture and dislocation."
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	"Know this, dear son, that foolish physicians neglect this chapter because they have never seen any of the ancient books or read a letter from them;"
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	"and for this reason, knowledge is lacking in our land, for I never found anyone skilled in it."
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	"I know nothing about it except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have practiced this art and gained experience through long practice;"
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	"And I have described for you in this chapter all that is contained therein, abbreviated at the end, and have clearly shown the shapes of the instruments used, as I have done in these two preceding chapters."
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	"It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the sums of our words and chapters where the wise devote their understanding and remain on the path of truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art and teach it to others."
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	"I say that when fracture, dislocation, torsion, or crushing occurs to anyone, you must quickly cleanse the wounded area on both sides if possible, especially if there is any weakness of the body, such as in children or the elderly;"
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	"or if the weather is not very warm or too cold; and avoid cold foods such as cold drinks, meat of poultry and rabbit, and do not drink wine or eat fatty meats that fill the veins with blood to the point that you doubt the formation of heat or the spread of matter in the limb. Let the patient return to their usual diet."
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	"And when the fractured bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that promote growth and have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, eggs, fish, and similar foods, along with abundant wine."
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	"For with this kind of nourishment, muscle tissue is regenerated and healing occurs more quickly."
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	"Know that the bones of the elderly and decrepit cannot be properly aligned and fused according to their nature due to the stiffness of the limbs, nor those that are too soft, such as the bones of young children;"
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	"but take care to bind the fractured bone with a large splint that fits and joins the limb together until it regains its former strength. Do not attempt to set the bone perfectly, but rather feed them on nourishing foods as we have mentioned."
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	"And know that fractures are diverse in many ways."
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	"For a fracture of the head is different from one of the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manner of fractures."
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	"There are fractures that occur suddenly, like when falling from a height, and others that occur gradually, such as carving a quill for writing."
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	"And there is fracture with wounding, and fracture with just a slight crack."
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	"Each type has its own method and appropriate instrument for restoration, according to how the injury presents itself;"
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	"And a fracture of the bone is known by the twisted appearance of the area and can be felt through the skin when pressed with the hand;"
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	"and if there is no twisting or sound when touched, and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no fracture."
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	"But there may still be twisting, cracking, or a small fracture present."
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	"So do not move the limb by hand but apply the medicines mentioned below and then gently immobilize it."
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	"And know that fractures occurring from falls are composed of two disjoined parts, which must be aligned precisely before heat arrives;"
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	"and if heat comes quickly, wait a few days until the inflammation subsides;"
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	"then align the limb gently and steadily, knowing that restoration is easier when there are no fragments. Then immobilize it as described below."
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	"And if the bone is broken in pieces, they should pull it apart into two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or with your hand if it's a small limb, or with two cords, or with one cord and your hand."
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	"And put the limb back in its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken limb are aligned, fix them firmly in their places with all your strength, and ensure that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient."
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	"And join the two ends of the bones together according to the best forms."
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	"Moreover, one can feel it well with the hand if it seems not to be in its proper place; raise it gently and do not strain or press it too much as those who cause heat and tension in the limb through their work."
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	"And once the limb is set properly, one should admonish the patient not to move it either while awake or asleep, nor while turning or in any other manner."
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	"Make sure that the limb is secured so that the patient feels no pain."
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels any pain, then it is not properly set, and one must arrange him in such a way that he feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	"And ensure that it is placed correctly so that there are no distortions when it is restored."
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	"And the qualities of a broken limb are as I have told you."
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	"Know that broken limbs vary in size, shape, and extent."
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs like arms and hands and suchlike which must be wrapped in soft and fine linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	"And those that are large like thighs and legs should be wrapped with a broad and hard bandage because wide bandages encompass the whole limb evenly and compress it equally on all sides so that there is no slackness."
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then tie it around with light pads, three or four turns depending on the limb, and tighten your hand a little on all of the bandage. Then go above the break and tighten less so that the break can separate a little;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the bandage bit by bit until you grasp much of the sound flesh, then take another bandage and wrap it again around the broken place;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the break and tighten it moderately, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said before in the first binding;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the bandages wads of linen or cloth so that it is all even, then tie everything with one bandage on top and then place your well-made splints on if there is no wound or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or inflammation, place over it something that calms heat and reduces swelling, and leave it like this for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then tighten over your splints with half of a wide cane jointed together tightly or with wood used for hoes or palm ribs, and let them be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But the bandage that is placed on the fracture must be somewhat thicker and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And it should also be as long as necessary for the limb's size or length;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then press on the stars likewise as you did for the first bandage, then bind above with running thread just as in the first bandage on the fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	More tightly woven afterwards, less so; and it is necessary that the thread be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as I have seen in some foolish people's work who use twisted cord for their bandages, and that is a great mistake; for the wrapping cannot be even if it is too delicate, nor should there be more than two spaces between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the edges of the stars after binding in sound places, then place underneath them lint or woolen bandage so that he does not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When there is a wound with the fracture and the bones are broken, I will speak of its treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that one must not bind all broken members with stars on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the member is large, one must not put on stars until after five or seven days, or more, according to the certainty of a hot aposteme appearing;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the manner of ancient emplastes for restoring fractures, dislocations, and distortions: Take flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of eggs, and make this mixture, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common manner of the restorative emplaste for fractures in many dispositions, especially for women and young children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of emplaste restoring fractures and dislocations and distortions: Take aloes and ladanum and fennel and asarabac and tragacanth and myrrh and aloewood, all together nine parts; mastic three parts; aloechy three parts; and make powder of them, and mix with plenty of eggs; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this emplaste, for it has good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is useful to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of emplaste that is useful for distortions: Take tragacanth and bdellium, each nine parts; myrrh and aloeswood, each eight parts; acacia six parts; bolus armeniacum ten parts; grind well and mix with water or plenty of eggs, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another manner of emplaste for joints and bones out of their places, and alleviates the pain that arises, and grinds down bone, and fractures: Take new wool, wet it in warm water and oil, and put it on the place. This emplaste does not restore, but is good for alleviation of hot aposteme, and removes pains properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth peony leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to facilitate removal of the bandage. Take equal parts root of marsh-mallow, camomile flowers, violet blossoms, wheat flour; grind them together, mix with wine, and if the limb is inflamed, mix with coriander water or water, and use accordingly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of plaster more powerful than the first, when hard swelling comes to the restoration of the limb. Take equal parts root of marsh-mallow, linseed, balm, melilot, hyssop, violet blossoms and camomile flowers; grind them together, mix with salt water or fresh water or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not apply anything to a broken limb for restoring strength besides wax and oil ointment; he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And according to Galen, one should apply slightly warm dry substances like myrrh, aloe, frankincense, and similar things to a broken limb for restoring it, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat injury and pain is to take mastic, chewed barley grains or chicken feathers, and silkworms, crush them together with equal amounts of salt, and make an ointment from the mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then let it rest for a while afterwards, and make sure that the patient feels no pain or movement of the bone from its position; if not, do not remove the bandage for several days
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain or itching occurs at the site with no rest or swelling, quickly remove the bandage and the ointment; then take a light cloth and a damp sea sponge, soak it in water, and apply it to the area until the itching stops and the pain is relieved
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply dry linen moistened with rosewater or rose oil and bind it tightly until you are sure that a warm blister has formed
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the limb subside, and let the pain be relieved, then resume the gentle binding with a little ointment, but not as tightly as before; continue until it is completely healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the blister is hot, red, painful and swollen, has disappeared completely, and you still need ointment and bandages, then resume them again as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if none of the above occurs at the limb, do not remove the bandage until after 3 or 4 or 5 or even 7 days; sometimes leave it on for as many as 20 days, depending on what is seen, until the fracture has healed and the flesh has grown together again.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then bind more tightly than before and increase the flesh around it, as I said earlier. And if you see that the area is drying out too much, know that nutrition cannot reach it
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then apply warm water compresses every time you remove the bandage, once every third day, and loosen the binding slightly
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this treatment, nourishment will quickly reach the limb, and you will soon see the improvement that foolish doctors fail to achieve by twisting the limb. This is bad practice, and amounts to mere trickery; I know of no other way than to leave it alone and operate correctly
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various kinds of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many different kinds of fractures with varied appearances, each having its own distinct cause.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For example, fractures caused by a blow from a sword can shatter the bone all the way down to the marrow, like splitting wood with an axe. This type of fracture is called a "hache" or "axe wound".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone from above without piercing it, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute"; and wounds from these two fractures are large or small in size.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussive impact, such as striking with the butt of a rock, falling onto stone, or similar events.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the membrane beneath the bone or above it, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a fracture that enters the bone so subtly like a hair, and this break is small, for which reason it is called "hairline fracture".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by striking with a rock or falling, or by similar events, causing a fragment of bone to enter inward and become stuck there like a potter's tool when they strike pots.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in those who have moist heads with soft bones, such as children's skulls
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and occurs in all types of fractures where small fragments are dislodged like stars; I will speak about this later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all kinds of fractures by their withdrawal from the bone, and by careful examination, and by corrupted flesh that lies upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	A hairline fracture is recognized by the fact that when the bone is exposed and rubbed gently, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating a fracture, beware of possible complications such as vomiting blood, loss of consciousness, and extension of the limb, pallor, fever, eyes protruding or turning red, etc. If any of these occur, recovery will not be without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not observe any alarming complication, and you hope for a good outcome, then begin the treatment
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the injured person first comes to you, especially if it is wintertime, remove the bone within fourteen days after the injury.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is summertime, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the membrane beneath the bone does not become corrupted and the complications we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture extends to the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary to open up the broken part in this way: first take hold of the injured person's head and uncover the bone in every possible manner until you reach the wound itself. Then proceed gently along the edge of the wound
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if blood flows or a hot swelling appears when the bone is exposed, apply whatever aid is necessary. Then fill the wound with bandages moistened in rose oil
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and allow the wound to rest until the hot swelling is appeased and you are assured that there will be no further bleeding. Then begin to remove the bone in one of two ways: either cut closely along the edge of the bone with a chisel, like this:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	"And then I add another cut larger than the first."
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	"And the second way is that you have many different cuts, some narrow and others wide, pointed and made of tin, and work lightly so as not to injure the head."
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	"And if the bone is hard and rough, then you must pierce it around beforehand before administering cuts with trephines so that they do not go too deep and pierce through the soft bone. The point should have a margin or circle on top to prevent it from going too far into the bone; and you should have several trephines so that each one fits properly onto the radius of the bone, allowing for all types of bones."
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	"The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you place a trephine on the bone and turn it with both hands until you know that the bone is pierced. Then move the trephine to another spot a little later and do this all around, then cut away the space of bone between the perforations with scissors as subtly and lightly as possible so that you can easily remove the bone by hand or with any of your tools such as forceps; be careful not to touch the cerebellum or cerebrum."
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	"And once you have pierced and removed the bone, you must then use another tool similar to scissors but thinner and more delicate than regular scissors to remove the remaining sharp edge of the bone."
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	"And if there are no small bones or scales remaining, then remove them lightly with some tools. Then clean the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said."
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	"And another way of operating is that which Galen recommends, which is quicker; he praises it highly, and this is his opinion."
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	"Firstly, you must uncover a part of the bone where the fracture is most visible. Then, once this part has been uncovered, place the lenticular trephine on top of it, as shown below:"
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	"And do not cut on one side alone, for the bone is sharp on both sides. Thus, the cutting is towards the bone. Then strike lightly with a small hammer so that you gently tap around the bone, and beware of the flesh underneath."
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	"If it adheres to the bone, cut lightly, for one cuts well without harm or fear."
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	"And if the bone fracture does not reach the flesh, and the bone is cut only on one side with small fragments remaining, then you should remove this roughness. Use a fine rasp in various quantities to best fit the work and shape of the fracture."
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	"Use coarse rasps first, then finer ones, until it is smooth."
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	"For each of the other cuts and fine fractures, you must adapt your approach according to its direction; this is something that cannot be learned from those who have studied this art."
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	"And if the sinew is exposed, you must take a cloth of linen according to the size of the wound, soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound."
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	"Then take another cloth doubled in two or three layers, soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth. Do this as gently as possible to avoid straining the sinew. Then apply another bandage on top, but do not tie it too tightly."
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	"Leave it like this for one or two days until the inflammation has subsided. Then untie it and apply medicines such as lily root, white lead powder, incense powder, aloe, and similar substances. Make a powder from these ingredients and apply it to the wound, then apply ointments without causing irritation."
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	"And make sure the wound is always clean. Do not leave ointment on it, and do not allow bowels to accumulate there, as they would otherwise corrupt and putrefy, causing great harm to the patient. When something irritating is placed on sinew, it becomes necrotic above it."
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	"Therefore, if any bad accidents occur to the patient, as we have said, be very cautious and doubtful without doubt."
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	"And if blackness appears on the wound due to the medicine applied, you must take one part honey and three parts rose oil, mix them together with a cloth, and apply it to the sinew."
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Then follow the usual methods of treatment until he is healed."
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one alone, for they are two bones; and the lower one is cartilaginous and does not break unless struck or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must place your little finger or the tip of your nose on the break and hold it steady with your index finger and thumb until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, ensuring that the patient does not feel pain from your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and your finger cannot reach it, then you must place a small wooden stick against it to hold it steady.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two places, do likewise, and make haste to restore it on the first day if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling boil is quieted,
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you set one bone against another on the opposite side, if there is a fracture there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the holes of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some surgeons say that the bandages should be moistened with butter and changed every day. It does not seem right to me, but rather they should be moistened in a mixture of egg yolk and flour powder; then leave the bandage until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes feathers from a goose are used instead of bandages, and if there is one soft cloth around them, the fracture will stay in place and the patient will feel better; now do what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if any swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, then put cerate or cotton moistened in rose oil or in a drop of diachylon there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if swelling does not come to the nose, then put a plaster on it made of sesame flour and frankincense powder, cooked with egg yolk, then put light dressings on it, and do not bind the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the nose is small and it is broken into many pieces, then extract it with appropriate instruments, then sew up the split and heal it with things that bring together flesh and bone, such as plasters and salves appropriate for this purpose.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the nose, then heal it with bandages and put in splints of plaster until it is well.
de la routure de la mandibule	de la routure de la mandibule
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken underneath and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is only apparent and not broken in two pieces except for small fragments inside, then it is easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary that if the fracture is on the right side, you put your two index fingers in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, then put your two index fingers of the right hand inside gently and hold it with your other hand from outside and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced in two pieces, then you must apply traction from both sides until it is even and aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of teeth or fracture, then tie them with a thread of gold, silver or silk, then put cerate on the broken jawbone and put a double cloth over it; then put a large well-made bandage or a piece of leather the same size as the jawbone, long and wide according to the jawbone, and tie it under the chin that you can see, and command the patient to rest and chew light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then untie it on the third day and then put back in place what has changed; then put a plaster made of flour with egg yolk or sesame flour after removing the cerate; then put light linen over the plaster, and if the plaster dries up and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it is well; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, then apply what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both fracture and wound together, be sure that no piece of bone has been taken out. Then carefully extract it with appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with fire according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And when you have removed all these fragments, and none remain, then stitch the wound, if it is wide, and apply one of the suitable emplasters to cauterize, so that it may heal."
de la forcele	"with great strength"
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceful blow strikes several times before, toward the shoulder, and the break is in one of three ways: either it is broken and dislocated in two places, with fragments, which is easiest to reset; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the treatment is when the break is without wound, that you have two assistants: one holds the arm that feels the force of the break; and the other extends the neck towards the part. Then place the break evenly in your two hands, so that the form is as it should be, neither twisted nor crooked.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place under the shoulder of the patient a round pad made of cloth or wool, and it should be thick according to your need. Then stretch and lift the forceful blow, and hold the pad with your hand so that you can set the break evenly as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forceful blow outward because it comes from deep inside, then the patient must lie on their back with their shoulders hanging down, and place a medium pillow under the shoulder. Then have the assistant push the shoulder downward until the bone of the forceful blow is lifted up.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then align the break with your two hands, and if it is misaligned, you must cut upward. Then pull out the fragments gently, and if the bone cannot meet due to any obstacle, then use one of the chisels that you have to scrape it away. But place this instrument under the forceful blow to ward off the sinews.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And it should resemble a spoon and not be sharp, and be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the power of the work. And it should have two sides, one wide and one narrow, like the shape of the wound you made when you exposed the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And once you are sure of hot inflammation, then close the wound. And if the opening is small or you doubt hot inflammation, then fill the wound with bandages and gauze according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot inflammation comes, then soak a bandage in rose oil mixed with honey and vinegar and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The bandaging of the bone when there are no wounds or incisions is done by placing on the bone a plaster made from the powder of millstone and egg whites. Then place light dressings on top, and if necessary, place a pad under the elbow.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very wide bandage about a palm's width, then place a doubled gauze on top of the dressings and plaster. Then take a narrow strip about three fingers' width and long enough to wrap around the bandage so that the ends hang down.
