et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	Then place the strip on top of the break, and twist the bandage over the neck, under the healthy shoulder, and under the injured shoulder. Then wrap each side separately, and when you see that the wrapping holds the break securely in place, and you can clearly see that the strip does not move on top of the broken bone, then renew it every day. And when the wrapping becomes loose, then tighten it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	And have the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the shoulder while they sleep to lift the arm up high. This will help alleviate the strain on the break by aligning the shoulder, or you can tie the arm to the neck and leave it tied for twenty days unless some misfortune happens.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then restart the plastering if necessary, and continue to wrap it tightly until it is healed. This usually takes about twenty-eight days, but for some people it may take less time.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Regarding the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It may happen that the shoulder bone breaks or is dislocated from its middle and cannot be seen except by touch. So arrange it according to the shape of the break, and wrap it according to its natural form in every way possible. Then place on the bone powder from a millstone mixed with egg whites, and light dressings, then place a doubled gauze on top. Then place a wide and thin strip over this, somewhat wider than the shoulder. And if there are sharp points under the strip in any part of the shoulder, fill those areas with linen pads so that the strip lies evenly. Then bind it tightly with a wide bandage so that the strip does not move from its position. Check the wrapping every day, and whenever it becomes loose, tighten it again, and if the strip has moved from its place, reposition it, and have the patient lie on their side. The shoulder is usually healed in twenty to twenty-five days. And when this time has passed, untie it, but be sure, for this is not a bone that heals easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone sticks out in front and there is nothing under it to support it, then cut it off and do what we have said for healing hot inflammation in cases of shoulder dislocation.
de la brisure dou pis	Regarding the break of the arm
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The arm bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens infrequently. However, it often breaks at the elbow. When it breaks in the middle, it drops downwards and the patient feels great pain, nausea, faintness, and may even vomit blood. The sharp points of the broken bone can be felt under the skin, and it is very painful to touch them.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the healing of this break is as follows: have the patient lie frequently on their back with a pillow between their shoulders. Then press down on the shoulders and bring together the ribs of the two sides at the hands using all possible care to make the bone figure straight. Then place plasters and dressings on top of a thin strip of salt or light wood, wrap it in a cloth, and tie it onto the broken bone so that it does not move. Wind the wrapping around the back and bind it firmly, checking the dressing every hour. If it becomes loose, tighten it again. If it needs to be untied due to corruption, itching, pain, or inflammation, do so quickly and remove the plaster. Then redo the plaster and binding as needed until the bone is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Regarding the break of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that rib fractures only occur in the thick parts near the back and at the front of the chest, and they only bend when they are brittle. The pain is felt sharply with each breath two fingers' width from the spine.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the healing of this break is to align the break properly, then place plasters and bind it with a strip if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is angled inwards, the patient feels intense pain and sharpness like that of pleurisy, because the bone is pressing on the lung. The patient may have chills, faintness, and vomiting a large amount of blood, which indicates serious condition. In ancient times, this was considered very dangerous.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	"Moreover, there are those who say it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly to reduce displacement."
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	"We do not do this, unless highly skilled physicians have come and seen it firsthand."
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	"And if it has come, then heal it."
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	"And they said that one should apply cupping jars to the place to draw out the moisture strongly, and this seems reasonable. However, there is doubt as to whether the cups will actually draw out the excess fluids due to weakness of the body."
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	"And they said that one should cover the place with wet wool in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to hold it evenly in place. Then treat it with the cure for pleurisy using meat and medication."
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone sticking out of the flesh, then doubt may arise in the patient whether one should cut through the skin above the broken rib and place some instrument underneath to ward off the spleen. Then one must chop away the bone lightly and gently pull it out, and stitch up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and dress it with poultices until it is healed. And if inflamed pus comes, then put wet cloths soaked in rose oil on it and place them on the area. Then treat the area according to what is needed for an inflammation, and keep lying on the side where it should be, until it is healed."
de la brisure dou col	Here's how you can ask about "la brisure du col" (the fracture of the neck) in Old French:
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes breakage occurs at the bones of the neck, rarely does it bend; likewise at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover or not, take note if you see their hands softened and swollen and numb, and cannot move or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it. Know that in many cases it is mortal, and if they move and feel well when pressed and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if cared for properly.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will recover or not, take note if the feet are softened, and if the accident is present in the hands, and wind passes involuntarily and exits through the back; and when one is lying on their stomach, wind passes involuntarily. And when they lie on their back and want to raise themselves up, they cannot. Know that it is mortal: do not waste time in treating it.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not occur, then the condition is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that if there is a hot inflammation, you should apply rose oil or oil of mallow seed to the spine until it is cooled down. Then apply a comforting and drying emplaster, secure it with a linen bandage, and command the patient to rest; and they should not sleep on the part where they feel pain until they are recovered.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, you must couch the patient on their back. Remove the displaced bone and then bring together the two lips of the wound if it is large by sewing them up with a suture. Then treat it with ointment for wounds until healed. And if the joint of the bone is broken, which is called the “joint of the cow,” you should put your left hand pouch in place of the bone and support it with your other hand using all your strength. Then apply the emplaster and bandage if necessary, bind it tightly, and if there are displaced bones, open them up and remove them, then treat the wound until healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Regarding the fracture of the thighbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens rarely that the thighbone is broken, and if it does happen, there will be a slight loss of consciousness at the head. The wound opens up lengthwise and slopes towards the knee, causing pain and sharpness in the area where it has been broken. Swelling occurs where the bone has snapped.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you should extend your hand over the break until you are able to locate it. Know what type of fracture it is and its shape. And if the fracture is only at the top, then bring the fracture into alignment so that it is in its natural position.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise or slopes inward, have the patient lie on their stomach so that you can see the alignment of the fracture clearly.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And once you have aligned it, apply an emplaster and then place a splint made of wood or bone. Bind the fracture tightly so that it does not move, and support the area below the hips until the alignment is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if there is an inflammation around the wound, do not touch it until the inflammation has subsided. Then apply what was mentioned earlier and return to the reduction of the fracture, binding it as necessary if there are no complications. This is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Regarding the fracture of the humerus
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The humerus is the bone between the elbow and the shoulder joint. If it is broken, it should be reduced in one of two ways:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie two joints with two strings,
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	"And the other manner is thus: place the patient on their back, and have them raise their hand to their neck. Then command two ministers: one shall grasp what is above the fracture at their hands, and the other shall grasp below at just one line, each stretching according to their part."
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	"And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then bind one line below the fracture and another above it, each minister stretching according to their part. And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, you must place one line in the middle below the axilla and another towards the side, below the fracture; likewise if the fracture is towards the side, you must place one line gently without straining until the fracture is level on its place and on the side. Then set the fracture level as it should be, and bind it, so that no inflammation occurs."
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	"And if inflammation occurs, do not bind until it has subsided for seven days. Apply a damp linen cloth moistened in axle oil and rose oil until the inflammation has decreased. Then bind as follows: place the splint on the fracture, bring the arm up to the sling, and place your hand on the shoulder or breast. Place the bandage and bind over the sling and arm so that the arm is in line with the stars, unless something prevents it from doing so, or if the bone has been moved."
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	"And if you suspect that the bone is not setting properly, use stars and place a larger and stronger one on the fracture than the others. Place two fingers' width between each star, and let each star be so large that it extends three fingers beyond either side of the fracture. Then bind over the stars as I have described at the beginning of this chapter, binding more firmly and not allowing any separation."
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	"And if you see that the stars and the bandage are in place as we have described when reducing the broken limb, but you suspect inflammation, let it rest for seven days as we have said. Then examine the bandage every three days to ensure that there is no pruritus, swelling, or redness around it, or that the limb does not become numb due to being too tight. Then adjust it as we have described."
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	"And if no such accidents occur, do not remove the bandage until three days or more have passed, and let the patient lie on their back with their hands on their stomach. Place one pillow of equal thickness beneath the sling to keep the figure of the broken limb still and prevent the binding from loosening. Watch the limb every hour during the day or night to ensure that it does not move or become loose. Adjust it as necessary using medicinal remedies, and feed the patient according to our previously stated method, ensuring that the food is initially soft and later more substantial as they begin to recover. It is customary for slings and splints to be used for forty days in total before removing them and applying baths and ointments to help heal the limb. If the fracture is severe and displaced, it may take up to ten days or two months to remove the bandage."
de la brisure du bras	Here is a summary of the instructions given for reducing and immobilizing a broken arm:
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones called the "fuscile," one of which is small and guides the wrist; the other is large and located beneath it near the little finger. Sometimes only the large bone breaks, or sometimes only the small one does, but sometimes both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bone is broken, its restoration is easy, and its healing; but when the large one is broken, its healing is poor, and more painful than when both are broken together. If it is only the small bone that is broken, then it should be gently straightened and set even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bone that is broken, then one must pull more strongly; and lay it out on one cushion, and stretch the pouch of the hand higher than the other fingers, and let the little finger be lower than the others, and have the patient lie across themselves with one cushion in front of them higher up so that the patient suffers no labor. Then extend the minister's upper arm to the part below the patient's hand or to one elbow, and another minister to the other above it. And then let the doctor set it even according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces missing, then place each one back in its proper position; and if there is any bone that cannot be grasped by the hand, and you are unable to restore it to its place, then saw through it and join the bones together, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is also an open wound with the fracture, I have spoken about that in the chapter on open wounds; take care accordingly.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if there are hot swellings at the beginning of the setting process, then put on one bandage of cerote made from rose oil and white wax; not too hard or too soft; and tie one bandage lightly until the hot swelling is alleviated. Then remove the cerote, and place the plaster for the mill powder with plenty of egg; then put on the splints, and let the splint be stronger than the others at the fracture, but a little wider; know that it must have six splints for the arm in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and tie more tightly at the fracture than elsewhere, tying less tightly as you move away from it, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the bandages that are on the fracture be soft and moistened, not hard or harsh; and let the thread for tying be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And examine the limb and the dressing after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if some bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you should bathe the limb with warm water until the itching is alleviated; and let the limb rest not too tightly. Then begin the bandaging again, and if the dressing has loosened and the bones have separated, and suchlike things happen, address them accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take care that the swelling does not come to the limb because it is too tight, then you should soften it a little and leave it thus for a few days until the swelling has gone down, then tie it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things that we have said happens to the sick person, then do not untie it for up to 20 days or thereabouts; then when he can put his hands around his neck and his collar bones are level, and take care against movement and dislocation, and sleep on his back; know that this fracture is healed in 30 days or 35, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the compositions and temperaments of the humors.
de la brisure de la main	Chapter on the Fracture of the Hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand and the back of the wrists there are few fractures, but many twists occur there.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or twisted, then let the patient sit cross-legged and sit upright before him evenly; then place his hand on the table, and extend the fractured bones, and align them correctly with the help of the surgeon until they are properly joined together; then apply the plaster and splints, if there are no wounds, then apply a bandage according to the size of the wound; and wrap it in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	"And if the break is on the outside around the belly of the foot, make a bandage of cloths and command the patient to bind it to their broken foot; then bind with a long cloth strip, and let the knot be soft as large as the sole of the hand, and bind it tightly."
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	"And if the break is on the front, then you must place a bandage above it and another below in the sole so that the hand is open and straight; then bind it all around the hand, and secure the knot between the two."
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	"And if the break comes on any of our fingers, if it is the thumb, then set it equal as it should be; and bind it with the sole, and if you see fit place a small straight bandage to raise the broken part, and do not move it. And if the break is on another finger, such as the index or one of the others, then set it equal, and bind it with the healthy finger that follows; or bind them all together in one bandage, whichever is better, or place a bandage like that on the thumb, and take care in the healing and arrangement of hot poultice, and treat what comes from it as I have said."
de la cuixe brisie	"for a broken thigh"
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it can be seen when it turns front and back; and its restoration is done by binding one bandage above the break and another below."
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	"And the patient lies on their face, then each helper extends their bandage to their side evenly; and this is when the break is in the bone."
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	"And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one bandage should be on the side towards the knee, and the other bandages below the break. And likewise if it is near the knee, and then the bandage should be near the knee, with the extension downwards; then the physician puts the bone in place with his two hands until it is according to its natural shape, and then places the splint and the bandage, if no hot poultice comes from it."
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	"And if there is a hot poultice, let it cool down and then return to your task and care; the bandaging is done in this manner."
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	"It is necessary that you wrap around the break one hard bandage doubled in two or three, and remove the excess, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the nape, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, with both ends coming out on top; then wrap the bandage up the leg and thigh, then place splints over the break, and place one splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and thigh with soft cloths to ensure an even binding, then begin to tie firmly three or four turns above the break, and as you go higher up from the break, tie less tightly; then take both ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and thigh, and tie three splints that are on top, then return down to the bottom end of the thread until you reach the foot; and bind it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like that until there is no poultice or swelling or other appearance."
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	"And if something comes from it, untie it and address what comes as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone sticking out, then remove them if possible; and if not possible, then cut open the space and extract it; and treat it as we have said until it is healed."
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	"And sometimes the thighbone breaks in such a way that splints are placed on it, like in the case of the arm; nonetheless, with this kind of treatment, the patient does not limp."
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	"And know that the thighbone is restored in one week, or a little less or a little more, depending on the different constitutions."
de la ruelle dou genoil	"of the crease of the knee"
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	You know that in the bend of the knee there is little breakage, but it folds many times. And if it breaks, it is only a crack, or one hole, and this happens to every wound, and without wound, and this is well known.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the reset is done by placing what is round on its two sides until it can be moved together; then put the bandage, and put a round splint if you need one, and bind it as necessary; then check all the arrangements that we have mentioned in other fractures, such as heat and similar appearances; then apply to each accident whatever is needed until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	You know that the leg has two bones, one of which is called by right "tibia", and the other is called "fibula"; and all other fractures come to it as they do to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is done in the same way as for the arm, and the work is the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg twists all around.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fibula is broken, it twists forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the tibia is broken, there is great pain and it is easily seen; and it twists downwards. Therefore arrange for traction, place it evenly, and tie the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the fracture is ugly and has many pieces, then traction should be less and lighter; and align according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, then take two strips of flexible wood that wrap around the leg on both sides and are long from the knee downwards; then wrap these two strips with two bandages above and below, and tie them in the middle as well, so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left at this joint, and this is good. And some arrange a splint of wood the length of the leg, and place the leg on it to prevent movement, and this is done properly when there is a wound near the fracture; and move the leg every day to see if there is heat or other accident; then treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fractures of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but sometimes a fracture comes to the bones of the foot and to the toes, and there is only shaking in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bones of the foot, and you see these bones protruding one over the other, then place your foot on the ground like someone who wants to walk, and then place your foot on theirs where the bones are raised, and press until they return to their places; then apply the splint and dressings, and put a small table with two holes under the sole of the foot, and then bind it tightly around the foot, and wrap it with bandages and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the toes are broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the broken toe and a little wider, then place that table I spoke of under the foot and bind it tightly; and if there are two or three or more broken toes, then place a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the table under the foot; and let them stand on top of the table so that they touch the sole of the foot well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And do not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, and treat each accident according to its need.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the fracture of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the wrist is broken in a woman, make her sit upright and incline her towards the back and have her held from behind; then fill the palm with cotton and put as much as one egg into it; then lift up the woman little by little from the back until the cotton comes to the entrance of the vagina and the bone returns with the egg. And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven days or so: then the fracture will be restored; and if you see that the palm is still not healed, take a sheep's bladder and tie a tube to its opening and put the whole bladder inside the vagina; then blow into the tube strongly until the bladder is full inside; then fill it with cotton and leave it like this for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the wrist of the man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the bone of the thigh; and these fractures near the hand are not hidden from those who study and practice this art, and understand my book. For the fracture indicates in many positions the right way to restore: therefore understand it.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's craw and put the penis into it; then wrap bandages around it and leave it for three or four days or so, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the hip or shoulder or similar, that he be cauterized immediately, so that the cauterization which we have described may testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, then apply the plaster of vitriol, or whatever else you have, and then begin to reset the fracture at that same hour, or on that day, if there is no inflammation.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if inflammation is present, then leave the reduction until a new day, until the inflammation has subsided, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would thereby cause harm.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone which has been broken appears above the exposed heart, then it is necessary that you put it back together lightly with your hands, using slight traction.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if traction does not allow you to align the bone ends with your hands, then use this tool made of iron, which is 27 or 28 inches long and its width corresponds to the size of the wound; and for that reason it is necessary for the surgeon to prepare three or four of them, according to what he needs in each case of fracture, and they should be round and somewhat thick so that they do not bend under pressure on the member where you are working, and they should have a pointed end at the front, and be thicker in the middle, as follows:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And this tool is called a "palm" because it must be placed on the head of the exposed bone; and strike it once, until it becomes straight, so that one end may align with the other. And if the fracture is very small and the tool cannot grasp the bone well, then you must cut off the end of the bone so that the tool can have better purchase.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you are unable to reduce the bone as we have described, then cut off a piece of an appropriate tool, such as a chisel or scalpel, with all your might; then remove the rough edges and small splinters that remain on the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone has been reduced and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position. Then do whatever is necessary to place it properly, then moisten a cloth with black stiptic wine and apply it gently if it is summer; and do not put any cerate or other oily substance on the wound, for it would cause decay and corruption. Then apply splints once you have reset the bone, and leave the wound open, and cut away all the surrounding skin according to the size of the wound, but be careful that the wound is not constricted with the fracture; many foolish physicians have done this and caused harm or death to the patient, so let the bandage be softer and gentler than usual for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large and you suspect that some mischance may occur, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then do not apply splints but wrap it tightly with hard cloths and tie them. And when you see after one or two days that the wound has begun to swell, then remove what you had put on with wine and apply healing ointment such as tetrafarmakon ointment or similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to dress the member twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is united and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the member be positioned in such a way that the bowstring runs smoothly downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and the bone still cannot heal but continually swells up again, know that there are small pieces of bone present which cause this pain. Therefore, you must probe the wound with a tent and remove all these unwanted pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula appears at the site or some other type of corruption, then you must treat it according to what is said in its chapter above. And when the bone is broken and exposed on the member, such as the hip bone or the upper arm bone and others similar ones of the large members, do not draw it out for many times the flesh will come off, but let it remain until it rots away; perhaps it will fall off by itself after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Chapter on fractures that occur on the union
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Many times, after the healing of a fracture, especially when it is near a joint, the appearance of the limb is unpleasant to see, and sometimes the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore be careful if the nail is fresh: you should administer stypptic medicines such as aloes, frankincense, myrrh, and sarcocolle, acacia, and similar others. Take some of these things or all together and combine them with stypptic wine or with egg yolk or with mustard; put them on the wound in poultices and tie it tightly, not untied for many days; then remove it and begin again another one until the node has been removed. Or you can apply a well-made piece of lead; for the property of lead is to remove all swellings from the limbs. And if the node has already turned into hardness like stone and needs to be removed, then cut it open above and remove the excess apparent matter. Or you can have it shaved by some barber until it is removed, then treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Chapter on members that are weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone has been restored and afterwards the member remains weak and thin, this happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was tied too tightly, and not tied as it should have been. Or because there were too many bandages, and the nourishment could not reach the member. Or because of excessive bleeding. Or because of too much movement, not at the right time. Or because there was little blood in his body, so he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is to make the patient eat well and exercise his body so that blood is multiplied in him. And administer baths, give him joy and amusement. Then apply pitch on the member so that it attracts great nourishment, and frequently anoint it with warm water until nourishment reaches the member, and return it to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Chapter on members twisted after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration,
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	"And dislocation may occur from continuous and prolonged rubbing with moist hands."
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	"And if the tortuosity is hardened and calcified like stone, so that it needs to be cut away with iron, then one must cut through it up to the bone with a fine, light scalpel. And take care and apply oneself in the treatment."
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	"Here begins the book of dislocations."
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	"A dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its proper place, preventing it from moving; the limb is misaligned and the patient feels great pain and injury."
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	"When dislocation occurs in someone, it must be reduced without delay."
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	"For if one delays, the place becomes inflamed and sometimes it cannot be put back into its proper position; therefore, one should not move it while it is inflamed, for this often causes spasms and other pains."
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	"Nevertheless, when this happens, let the sick person rest until the inflammation has subsided, then raise the limb with warm water and oil, gently move it around, and treat each joint as they come back into their proper place."
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	"And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from head to foot."
des mandibules	"of the jaws"
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	"It happens rarely that the jaws become dislocated within themselves, and there are two ways in which both can be dislocated: either they are somewhat displaced from their proper places and softened somewhat; or else they are completely dislocated and hang down towards the chest, preventing saliva from entering the mouth, so that he cannot keep his mouth closed nor speak clearly."
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	"If the dislocation is slight, it can be reduced by several methods."
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	"And if it is complete and full-blown, you must reduce it quickly and without delay."
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in this manner the servant holds the head of the patient, and the master places a pouch from one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on two parts; and the other two hands are free to hold evenly; and instructs the patient to soften their jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the master makes it even until it returns to its place
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the return is difficult, especially if it's both jaws at once, then apply hot water and oil so that they move easily; do not force the return, as we have said
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned evenly and the patient's mouth closes without softening, then place moistened cloths made of cerate made from rose oil and wax on it, then tie it gently with soft bindings
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient sleep on their back with two pillows between their legs so that they do not move to the right or left and do not attempt to chew, but take soft food until the pain is gone and the jaws are healed
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then they may eat what they wish easily, and should not strain to open their mouth when eating or drinking until the jaw is fully healed and sound
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be properly reduced within an hour and are not returned to their places, then fever and trembling will ensue, and sometimes diarrhea and possibly vomiting of clear bile may occur
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see these signs, know that it is a lost case; and many times the person dies within eight days
de la forcelle	Of lockjaw
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	Lockjaw cannot be dislocated from the side inward and is sometimes dislocated downward; this can be felt
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the reduction is done by having the patient lie on their back with arms extended; then press firmly on the cheek with the palm of your hand and it will return to its place; then apply a plaster and bindage
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the jaw on the side towards the cheek cannot be dislocated; if it is, it will return to its place by itself, as we have said. Then apply a plaster and bindage and command the patient to rest until they are healed
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And likewise is the jaw on the spine returned to its place when it has been dislocated from its position
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated forward in three ways: one is at the part of the socket below; the second is at the part of the chest; and sometimes it is dislocated above, but this happens rarely
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And the shoulder does not dislocate backwards or inward through the nerves, but it often dislocates downwards towards the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, for then it jumps forth hastily; but in those with much flesh, it jumps hardly at all and returns quickly
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes some people suffer a blow or fall and the shoulder becomes swollen with a hot inflammation, and they think that it is dislocated because of this
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore you must examine it to make certain, and then begin treatment
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And a dislocation is known when it is downwards towards the socket, and a distinction can be made between the affected shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a noticeable difference between them
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder and below the socket to the touch as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring their hand near to their neck nor move in any way
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it clearly by touch
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this type of dislocation cannot be reduced unless it is recent or the patient is a child
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is for the practitioner to raise the patient's hand upwards and then place their fists underneath the socket and pull up forcibly with the joint until it returns to its place
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come back as we have said within a few days afterwards, then the patient should be bathed in warm water and given softening and soothing ointments such as decoctions of marshmallow, fenugreek, and mallows in water
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then let the patient lie on their back and place a soft cloth pad underneath the socket, not too soft nor too hard. Then the practitioner places their heel on the pad and raises the shoulder gently, while pulling the patient's hand towards them
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another practitioner holds the patient's head so that it does not move downwards; then this shoulder will come back suddenly, and if you wish to see how it is reduced in this manner
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	And it is that you have present one person who is taller than the patient and stands upright next to them, and places their shoulder underneath the socket of the patient's arm and lifts the socket upwards so that the patient hangs in mid-air
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another practitioner pulls the patient's arm downwards towards their belly. And if the patient is too light, then they should hang some heavy weight with them and the dislocation will return quickly
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And it is also reduced in another manner: and this is by planting a long stick into the ground so that its top is as high as the patient's elbow and not too thick nor too thin
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	And then place the patient's arm over it, but have soft cloths underneath them so that they are standing on the stick. Then stretch their hand downwards on the other side strongly and the joint will return to its place quickly
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And if it does not want to return by all the things that we have said, then do this treatment: take a stick of two spans long and four digits wide with a pointed end for entering deeply underneath the socket in this shape
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	And then place cloths over the top of the stick so that it does not bruise the patient and place it underneath the socket of the affected shoulder. Then extend your arm over the stick and attach the sling to it and to the elbow of the hand, then place the arm on a rung of a ladder of the same width and let the hand hang downwards and allow the body to hang on the other side; the joint will return now
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is back in place, however it may be, then you must place underneath the socket a wool pad of equal size and then apply the plaster prepared with powder from the millstone, with incense and egg white all over the shoulder and around it, then press it firmly underneath the socket and twist the bandage on the plaster and tie the hand to its neck in this manner
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that they eat little, so that the member is comforted because it will heal more quickly. And then later after five or six days they should eat more and move around, and if it becomes firm again without becoming softened, then it is healed
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has gone out of place due to moisture that has come or for another reason, then you must apply cauterization at three points as it is described in the chapter on cauteries
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	"And if you do all this and after seven days the joint still does not stay in place, and he cannot raise his arm above his head, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be set back in its proper place."
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	"If a dislocation occurs toward the elbow, breasts, or behind, it is made by forceful movement and stretching of the hands, and another ligature must be administered; treat until it is healed."
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	"And if after healing there comes stiffness in the limb and delay in movement, then the patient should use it many times until that stiffness is alleviated and returns to its original state."
de la dislocation dou coute	"of dislocation of the neck"
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	"Know that the joint of the neck is dislocated by force and returns by force; and if it is dislocated in all directions, especially front and back, and the dislocation has not been reduced, because one can see and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure."
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	"And when you join the sick neck with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly. For the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder at all."
