Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	"And it is necessary that you reduce it before any swelling occurs, for if swelling does occur, reduction will be difficult and perhaps not possible at all, especially when the dislocation is toward the back; this dislocation is worse than others and causes greater pain, and there may even be death."
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	"And the reduction is when it can be done so that you extend your patient's hand with both of yours; and let his arms be spread out, and place the joints of your hands on either side and above and below the neck, and press the joint into the patient's wrist or palm root until it returns to its proper place."
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	"And if the dislocation is toward the front, then it returns when you fold the hand onto itself and press firmly on the root of the palm where the neck is dislocated."
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	"And if it does not return to its place, then administer strong extension: have two ministers extend the arm and hold it so that it cannot move during extension. Then turn the arm on each side, after you have wrapped a long and wide cloth around it..."
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	"...and when the physician has joined the joint with his hand, he should anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then press the joint firmly until it returns."
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	"...and when it is in place, then put on a dry compress with egg yolk and press it firmly. Then wrap the arm around the neck of the sick person and leave it there for several days before removing it."
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	"And if the joint is firmly fixed in its place, then untie the bandage and leave it alone. And if you see that the joint is not yet well set, then start again with the compress and the bandage, leaving them on for several more days until it is firmly in place. Then remove them."
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	"And if the patient feels pain after reduction of the dislocation and the joint moves again, then bathe it and rub it gently, pressing until it is eased. Or you can put on a poultice of fresh sheep fat and leave it overnight for one day and night before removing it and immersing it in warm water..."
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	"...and when it is heated up, rub the joint moderately and then replace the poultice and immerse it in warm water again. Repeat this process two or three times until it is healed. And if you see fit, apply a moist compress of fine wheat flour mixed with butter and press it onto the joint to bring it back into position."
li dislocation de la main	Dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	"The dislocation of the hand is easy to reduce compared to other joints, but it must be done promptly as soon as it occurs before swelling sets in or heat comes."
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	"And the reduction is done by placing the affected hand on a table and having ministers extend it while the physician places his palm on the prominence of the joint and presses until it returns to its place."
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	"Nevertheless, you must always check if the joint is properly reduced. Then have the patient place the back of their hand on a table for extension and reduction."
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	"And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, then have the patient place their hand on the table with the back facing up. The physician should place his hand on the prominence of the joint. If it returns now, then it is well reduced."
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	"If not, then apply compresses with soothing poultices to draw out heat and leave them on without beginning again."
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	"And if the patient cannot tolerate it and you are unable to set the joint properly after several days, then the joint will remain dislocated..."
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	"...and it will harm the patient no further than while the hand is dislocated and unable to grasp anything at all: know then that the nerves or arteries have been severed, and there is no other remedy but to perform a cautery nearby, although sometimes nothing else can be done."
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	"And when the hand is in place, apply the compress that we have described, then bandage it and leave it for five days before removing it and leaving it alone."
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the hand cannot move properly and there is some pain, then apply hot water compresses and rub it until it is healed."
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of hand finger dislocations
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	"Sometimes fingers of the hand are dislocated on either side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the front."
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	"Then grasp the finger and push the dislocation back until it returns to its place. Then hold the base of the finger and bend it towards the part where it was dislocated..."
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	"...and leave it alone for two days before aligning it on the third day. Then bandage it as we have described and remove the bandage on the fourth day. Make sure to move the finger and then relocate it in place several times until it is well aligned."
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	"And do the same if it is dislocated on the front of the hand or any other side until it is healed."
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of dislocation of the shoulder blade bone__
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are many dislocations, there is no remedy, for the sick person dies quickly.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	The signs are that evacuations occur involuntarily and cannot be retained, and many times some limb is paralyzed, such as the two thighs or the two arms or one
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And often the spine moves in four parts; that which moves at the back is called "gilbosity":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The treatment is that if the gilbosity has come from childhood, there will be no remedy or cure for it at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from a fall or blow or similar things, the ancient authors propose many remedies in grand words, but they are not helpful in all cases.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	But I have shortened it according to my intention and formed various devices in different ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that for the gilbosity which comes at the front of the chest, there is no remedy or cure.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And likewise that which comes directly to both sides, and one can only cure the one that properly comes at the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And it is necessary for the sick person to be laid flat on his face in one even place, and have a board under him so that he does not break himself;
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then insert one stake into the head firmly in the ground, and another at the feet, and tie a rope around the patient's buttocks, and another at the hips, knees, and ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	And two ministers shall hold the limbs, one at the head and the other at the feet, amidst the two brands;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And let the brand be closed tightly as we have said, and let the surgeon place his palms firmly on the spine until it returns to its proper position.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a table three spans long, place it beneath the shoulder blade while the patient lies on their side, and insert the head of the table underneath the shoulder blade, then place the middle of the table on the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	Then the physician places their feet on the other head of the table and presses firmly until it returns to its proper place; if you see that this works, do the same for the dislocation that affects the hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	"And it is necessary that you insert two stakes into the head of the patient's arm, and two others toward the feet, with a handspan distance between each stake above and below."
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	"And in each stake there should be one hole through which the pin can turn, and the stakes should be firmly planted in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of stakes there should be one turning pin on which the cord will rotate, with two small pins a handspan long to turn the pin."
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	"And then tie the cord that is between the stakes to the pin near the head, and the other cord toward the feet to the other pin, and each of the assistants should turn their pin with all the cord, and the master should make the splint even as we have said."
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	"And once it is even, then place a dry compress with plenty of egg yolk on top, then the bandages, and then the splint made from a board three fingers long, placed to cover the area of the joint and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a cord as we have said, and let the patient be nursed carefully until they are well."
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	"And if any complication arises at the end of the healing process, then it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medications along with the splint that we have mentioned earlier; and sometimes one should apply a plaster."
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	"Furthermore, sometimes the appearance of a displaced vertebra in the lower back can give the impression that there is dislocation; however, this is actually the bone protruding, and one should not make assumptions about it, lest death ensue."
des dislocations de la hainche	"Displacements of the hip joint
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	"Know that the hip joints and shoulder joints only suffer dislocations, unlike other joints which can also experience fractures. The hip joint is dislocated in four ways: inward and outward, forward and backward; but more commonly inward than outward or forward and backward."
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	"And the sign of an inward dislocation of the hip is that when the affected leg is placed alongside the healthy one, it appears longer, and the knee joint on the affected side seems more prominent, and the affected person cannot bend their knee forward."
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	"And there is swelling with heat and redness at the spot where the hip bone has dislocated."
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	"And the sign of one whose dislocation is outward is that these accidents are opposite to those mentioned before."
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	"And the sign of one whose dislocation is forward is that they can stretch their leg well enough; nevertheless, they cannot bend the knee without pain, and if they try to walk, they cannot do so without difficulty, and they may retain urine, and the angle may be swollen, and when they walk, they tend to limp on the heel."
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	"And the sign of one whose dislocation is backward is that they cannot extend or bend their knee, and their leg appears twisted compared to the other one, and the angle is softened, and the hip bone is located below the ribs."
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	"The treatment for this type of dislocation is to wait and see if the dislocation is old, and if it remains in its position without causing any harm, then there is no need for treatment, and one should not make assumptions about it."
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	"And for those whose dislocation is recent and of the four types mentioned earlier, one should quickly reposition the joint by pushing it inward and outward, and moving it to the right or left; hopefully it will return to its proper place, and no further treatment will be necessary."
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	"And if the joint does not return to its proper place in this manner, then one must prepare an assistant and firmly grasp the leg with both hands or tie it firmly above the knee with a rope."
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	"And another assistant should extend their hand above in such a way that they place their hands beneath the buttocks, then quickly tie a soft rope around the hip bone, while another holds the end of the rope."
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	"Then all should pull simultaneously upwards and downwards until the affected person is lifted off the ground at once and remains hanging."
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	"This method of traction is suitable for all four types of dislocation, and if the joint returns to its proper place, as we have said, then that is good."
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	"But if the dislocation does not return to its proper place, then treatment should be tailored to its specific type. For dislocations that are inward, one must first turn the affected person onto their healthy side, then tie a rope around the root of the hip bone and the area below the angle, then pull the rope upwards towards the angle and the groin."
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	"Then another assistant should grasp the affected person's arms and embrace the large muscle of the thigh, pulling it strongly outwards: now the joint should return to its proper place. This type of dislocation is easier than the others."
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	"And if you are unable to reduce the dislocation in the manner we have described, then tie the two feet of the affected person together with a soft rope at the heels and knees, ensuring that the affected leg is extended about two fingers' breadth more than the other."
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	"Then hang the person from the top of a post, ensuring they are two arm-lengths above the ground. Then have one assistant embrace the head of the hip bone, and another assist the affected person by embracing the hip bone firmly, as the joint will now return to its proper place quickly."
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	"And when the dislocation is outward, have the affected person lie down as described earlier for those with coxa valga, and tie a rope around the affected leg properly and also around the foot."
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	"Then place two wedges under the head and another at the feet, then insert one wedge between the thighs of the affected person in the shape of a 'V'."
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	"And have moist cloths ready to prevent burning of the skin, then each assistant should pull in their own direction while the surgeon places his hand on the joint."
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	"If it returns to its proper place, that is good. If not, then have the person lie on their back and press down as described earlier for coxa valga, with the affected person lying on their healthy side."
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	"And when the dislocation is forward, quickly extend the affected leg as described earlier. Then place the surgeon's hand on the angle of the affected joint and press with the other hand while extending it downwards towards the knee."
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	"But if the dislocation is backward, do not extend the affected leg downwards or lift it up off the ground, but rather position the person as if they were sitting on their haunches, as described earlier for delivering a woman while seated on two stools."
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	"And have the person lie on their back with the rope extended as previously described, and then press down firmly on the joint using the table."
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	"And it will be complete when the affected person extends their legs and they are equal in length. Then bring the thighs together, apply the splint, and secure it with a bandage to prevent any movement of the hip."
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	"And after three or four days, remove the splint and replace it. If the legs are still equal in length, then secure it again as before and leave it for another three days. Then remove it and allow the person to walk slowly until they are comfortable."
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of knee dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The kneecap can dislocate in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	"And this sign is: instruct the patient to bend their leg towards their hip. If it does not align with their hip, know that it is dislocated."
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	"And the restoration of all this is: make the patient sit up straight, extend their leg if possible, and place your back against their face, with their foot on yours."
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	"Then take hold of their knee with your palms, pull it back between your two knees, and then bend both sides of the knee forcefully. Another assistant extends their foot until the kneecap returns to its proper place. The sign that it has been reset correctly is when the patient can easily align their leg with their hip."
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	"And apply the plaster on top, align the leg with the hip, and bind them together tightly for three or four days before releasing them. During this time, the patient should not walk until their limb has healed."
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And if the limb is not yet healed, use traction forcefully as we described in treating hip dislocation, until it is completely healed."
de la dislocation dou talon	"About dislocation of the ankle"
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	"The ankle is sometimes sprained and sometimes fully dislocated both inside and out."
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	"And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and it points forward at the part where it is dislocated:"
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	"The treatment for this is gentle traction, and one should gently extend the foot with their hands when it is only sprained."
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	"But when it is completely dislocated, make the patient sit up straight and have one assistant pull the leg forward above the ankle:"
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	"Then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, then your left twice, then extend it upwards and push the foot up into place;"
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	"and do this twice as described earlier by pushing and pulling the foot; if it goes back in properly, that's good. If not, start over again because sometimes it can go back in on its own."
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	"And if it cannot be reduced in this way, make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and firmly plant a pole in the earth between their thighs. Then tie the straps around so that they do not injure the patient."
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	"Then have an assistant pull on the thigh, and another assistant extend the foot with their hands or with a rope tied to the heel so that it hangs free:"
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	"then both assistants pull equally and keep the pole between the patient's thighs to hold them down while extending;"
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	"Then the surgeon places their hands equally on both sides of the dislocation, and another assistant pulls gently on the healthy leg below while the dislocation quickly reduces."
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	"And when it is in place, apply the plaster and bandages, tie them on tightly, bind the foot to the leg, and make sure that the ligaments behind the ankle are not too tight."
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	"Then leave it on for two or three days, and if the bandages loosen, retighten them. Remove them on the third or fourth day, and tell the patient not to walk for four days;"
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	"and if they walk before that time is up, there is a risk that it could dislocate again."
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"If inflammation sets in after the dislocation has been reduced, treat it as we described earlier until it is healed."
des dois	"about the toes"
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	"When the toes are dislocated, they should be gently extended without force, and this is an easy task."
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	"If the dislocation is located in any of the joints on the back of the foot, make the patient sit up straight on a chair or table and place your foot on the side of the dislocated joint. Then push down hard with your foot until it pops back into place."
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	"And once it is aligned and there is no gap, place a splint with two notches under the sole of the foot, tighten it, leave it on for three days, then remove it. Let the patient rest until they are healed."
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Concerning wounds and dislocations together:
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When dislocated wound occurs,
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not presumptuous in the treatment, if you are wise in the art and have practiced it for a long time, and if you are pitying, merciful, and careful, not hasty.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And first use soothing ointments to calm inflammation, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope of recovery.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	But if you do see hope, then quickly realign the limb before inflammation sets in
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And once the limb is back in place, administer soothing ointments for inflammation and treat the wound as necessary with drying ointments
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if there has been a fracture along with the dislocation, or small bones have been dislocated, then set them and do as we said for simple fractures
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	And keep yourself from fearing death, as I have said, for that would be displeasing to your Creator, and harmful to your soul and body. Amen
Explicit le romen de fisique	The end of the book of surgery
